درهم وان خاطـه غدا فله اجرة مثله عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله ولا يتجاوز به نصف درهم وقال ابو يوسف و محمد رحمهما الله الشرطان جائزان وايهما عمل استحق الاجرة ۱۹۹ (۴۴) وان قال ان سكنت في هذا الدكان عطارا فبدرهم في الشهر وان سكنته حدادا فبدرهمین جاز وای الامرين فعل استحق المسمى فيه عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله در ہم اور اگر سیا کل تو اس کے لئے اجرت مثل ہوگی امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور نہیں تجاوز کرے گی آدھے درہم سے۔ اور کہا صاحبین نے کہ دونوں شرطیں جائز ہیں اور جانسا عمل کرے گا اس اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا۔

A dirham, and if he sews it tomorrow, then he gets the like wage according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and it should not exceed half a dirham. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, said: Both conditions are valid, and whichever he performs, he deserves the wage. 199 (44) And if he said: If you place an attar in this shop then a dirham per month, and if you place a blacksmith then two dirhams, it is valid, and whichever of the two he does, he deserves the named wage according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. A dirham, and if he sews tomorrow, then for him is the like wage according to Imam Abu Hanifa, and it will not exceed half a dirham. And the Sahibayn said: Both conditions are valid, and whichever he performs, he will be deserving of that wage. Someone said to the hired worker: If you sew the cloth today, the wage will be one dirham, and if you sew tomorrow, the wage will be half a dirham. Then Imam Abu Hanifa says: If he does it today, it will be one dirham, and if he does it tomorrow, it will not be half a dirham; rather, the wage that is market rate for sewing that cloth will be given, but it will not exceed half a dirham. He says: 'If you sew today, one dirham' – this is for expediting, so the ijarah is valid, and if he sews today, he gets one dirham. But if he said 'if you sew tomorrow, half a dirham' – this is a suspension (ta'liq), and when the ijarah is suspended, the matter is not settled, so the ijarah becomes fasid. When ijarah is fasid, the rule is that the market wage is given, so the market wage will be given. But since half a dirham was agreed between them for sewing tomorrow, the market wage also does not exceed half a dirham. The Sahibayn say: Whether he puts the condition for today or tomorrow, both conditions are valid, so both ijarahs are valid. Thus, whichever act he performs, he gets the wage according to the condition. So if he sews today, he gets one dirham; if he sews tomorrow, he gets half a dirham. This issue is based on the principle that whichever condition of today or tomorrow is settled, that condition is valid and the ijarah is valid, and he gets the wage accordingly. [1199] (44) If he said: If you place an attar seller in this shop, then one dirham per month, and if you place a blacksmith, then two dirhams, then according to Abu Hanifa it is valid, and he deserves the named wage for whichever of the two he does. And the Sahibayn said: This ijarah is fasid. For example, Zaid leased a shop to Umar and said: If you let the shop be used for selling perfumes, the monthly rent will be one dirham; if you let it be used for blacksmithing, which is dirty work, the monthly rent will be two dirhams. Imam Abu Hanifa says both ijarahs are valid. So if he lets it for perfume, he gets one dirham per month; if for blacksmithing, two dirhams per month. In this case, the ijarah is not suspended; rather, it gives option between two tasks. Since both wages are clearly separate, the ijarah is valid. The wage will be according to the task performed. The determination of which task will be done happens at the start of work. This issue is based on the principle that if there are two distinct tasks and each has a known wage, the ijarah is valid. The Sahibayn say: At the time of contract, it is not known which task the hirer will perform, so the wage is not fixed—one dirham or two—so the wage is unknown (majhool), causing the ijarah to be fasid. Therefore, the ijarah is not valid, even if at the start of work it becomes known which wage applies. The principle is that if the wage is not known at the time of concluding the ijarah contract, the ijarah is fasid.
Source pages p. 204

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding two cases of ijarah with alternative wage conditions. In the first case, the employer says: 'If you sew the cloth today, wages are one dirham; if you sew tomorrow, wages are half a dirham.' Imam Abu Hanifa distinguishes: if the work is done today, the contract is valid and the named wage is paid because it's a condition for expediting. If done tomorrow, the condition is a suspension (ta'liq) making the contract fasid, so the wage is the market rate, not exceeding the agreed half-dirham. The Sahibayn consider both conditions valid, so the ijarah is valid in either case and the named wage applies. In the second case, the lessor says: 'If you place an attar in this shop, rent is one dirham per month; if you place a blacksmith, two dirhams.' Abu Hanifa again validates both because the contract gives an option between two specified uses with specified rents, so there is no uncertainty at contract formation—the work type is determined later but the wages are known. The Sahibayn rule it fasid because at contract time the rent is unknown (it could be one or two dirhams) and this uncertainty renders the contract void. The key point is whether the uncertainty (jahalah) is in the wage at the time of contract. Abu Hanifa focuses on the fact that both wages are specified in the contract; the Sahibayn focus on the lack of specification of which wage applies until later. The text notes that the first case (sewing) differs from the second because in the first the condition for tomorrow is a suspension, whereas in the second both options are equally possible from the start. The mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school is that ijarah with such alternative conditions is permissible if both wages are specified and the choice is left to the lessee/hirer, as per the later fatwa of many Hanafi scholars. However, the text here presents the dispute without giving a preference.

Key Terms
اجارة (ijarah): A contract of lease or hire where one party provides benefit/usufruct in exchange for a known wage
اجرت مثل (ujr al-mithl): The market rate wage for similar work, paid when the contract is fasid or when no wage was agreed
تعلیق (ta'liq): Suspending the effect of a contract on a future condition that may or may not occur; here, 'if you sew tomorrow' suspends the contract

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of renting a shop for either attar (perfume) or blacksmith use, why does Imam Abu Hanifa validate the contract while the Sahibayn deem it fasid?
A) Abu Hanifa considers the lessee's later choice as a specification of the contract, whereas the Sahibayn require the wage to be fixed at contract formation.
B) Abu Hanifa insists that the contract must be suspended (mu'allaq) to be valid, while the Sahibayn reject suspension.
C) Abu Hanifa thinks the wage can be decided after work starts, but the Sahibayn require it to be known before.
D) Abu Hanifa considers both tasks as one composite contract, while the Sahibayn see two separate contracts.

Key Takeaway
In ijarah, the validity of alternative wage conditions depends on whether the uncertainty is in the wage itself (jahalah) or in the choice between known wages; Abu Hanifa distinguishes between ta'liq and delegation of choice.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease
beginner
6 min
Renting 'Per Month' Without Total Term: Scope and Tacit Renewal
Ruling with proof on per-month ijarah without total duration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a rental contract where the rent is specified per month without a total duration, explain why the first month is valid, and describe how subsequent months can be renewed tacitly.

Core Idea
Renting at 'one dirham per month' without specifying total months is valid only for the first month.

This lesson examines a common scenario in rental contracts: the tenant agrees to pay a fixed rent 'per month' but no total number of months is mentioned. How does the Hanafi school treat such an arrangement? The answer hinges on the requirement that the duration of a lease must be known at the time of contract. The passage you are about to read from a Hanafi fiqh text clarifies the ruling and the mechanism by which the lease may continue beyond the first month through mutual tacit consent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract terms
The tenant rents a house for 'one dirham per month' but does not specify for how many months. This creates uncertainty about the total duration and total rent.
The rent per unit (month) is known, but the number of units is unknown.
2
Apply the condition of known duration
For an ijarah contract to be valid, the duration must be known and specified at the time of contract. Since only the first month is definite (one month), the contract is valid only for that month.
The first month has a clear beginning and end, and the rent for that month is fixed at one dirham.
3
Assess the remaining months
For months beyond the first, the duration is unknown at contract formation, so the contract is fasid (defective) for those months. However, the lease can continue through tacit renewal (bay' al-ta'ati) month by month if both parties act accordingly.
Tacit renewal means a new ijarah is formed each month by mutual conduct (e.g., tenant stays, landlord accepts rent without objection).
4
Note the proof (dalil)
The ruling is supported by analogy to a hadith prohibiting the sale of an unspecified quantity (heap of food), and an athar from Sufyan al-Thawri requiring known days and known daily allowance for a hire contract.
The key principle: jahalah (uncertainty) in the total duration or total wage invalidates the contract beyond the first definite unit.

(۱۲۰۰] (۴۵) کسی نے گھر کرایہ پر لیا ہر ماہ ایک درہم کے بدلے تو عقد صحیح ہے ایک مہینے میں اور فاسد ہوگا باقی مہینوں میں مگر یہ کہ تمام معلوم مہینے معن کر دئیے جائیں۔ کسی نے گھر کرایہ پر لیا اور یوں کہا کہ ہر ماہ ایک درہم کے بدلے اجرت دوں گا۔ تو ایک ہی مہینے کا اجارہ ہوا اگلے مہینے کا اجارہ نہیں ہوا۔ گھر والا اگلے مہینے اجرت پر دینے سے انکار کر دے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح کرایہ دار اگلے مہینے اجرت پر لینے سے انکار کر دے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اگلے مہینہ بھی رہنا شروع کر دے اور گھر والا کچھ نہ کہے تو یہ از سر نو اجارہ ہوا جو معروف طریقے پر گویا کہ اشارے اشارے میں بیع تعاطی کے طور پر ہو گیا۔ اور اسی طرح جتنے مہینے بغیر انکار کے رہتے رہیں گے ہر ماہ نیا اجارہ ہوتا چلا جائے گا۔ اور جس دن گھر والا یا کرایہ دار اجرت دینے یا لینے سے انکار کر دے اسی دن اگلا اجارہ ختم ہو جائے گا۔ ہاں ! تمام مہینے متعین کر دے تو جتنے مہینے متعین کرے گا اتنے مہینے کی اجرت ہوگی۔ مثلا دو سال طے کیا تو دو سال کا اجارہ ہوگا۔ تمام مہینوں کو طے نہیں کیا تو کتنے مہینے کا اجارہ ہوگا یہ مجہول ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ ہر مہینہ ایک درہم کا بول چکا ہے اس لئے اقل درجہ ایک مہینہ کا اجارہ ہو جائے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن الشورى في رجل يكترى من رجل الى مكة ويضمن له الكرى نفقته الى ان يبلغ قال لا الا ان يوقت اياما معلومة وكيلا معلوما من الطعام يعطيه اياه كل يوم (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل یکترى على الشيء المحمول وهل يجوز الكراء ادیا خذ مثله منه؟ ج ثامن ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۴۹۳۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تمام دن متعین کر لئے جائیں اور ان کے تمام کرائے متعین نہ کر لئے جائیں تب تک اجارہ صحیح نہیں ہے (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ ڈھیر کی مکمل مقدار معلوم نہ ہو تو اس کے بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے اس طرح تمام مہینے معلوم نہ ہوں تو ان کا اجارہ درست نہیں ہوگا حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت جابر بن عبد الله نهي حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی کسی آدمی سے مکہ تک کرایہ کے لئے لے اور مکہ تک پہنچنے تک اجیر کے نطقے کا ضامن ہوتو فرمایا یہ بھی نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ دن متعین کرے اور کھانے کا کیل معلوم ہو جو ہر دن دیگا ۔
And they (the Sahibayn), may Allah have mercy on them, said: The ijarah is fasid. 1200 (45) And whoever rents a house for one dirham per month, the contract is valid for one month and fasid for the remaining months, unless he specifies the total number of months as known. Therefore, the ijarah will be valid. And whatever work he does, he gets that wage. The determination of what work will be done will happen at the start of work. So this issue is based on the principle that if there are two separate tasks and each has a known wage, the ijarah is valid. The Sahibayn say: At the time of the ijarah, it is not known which task the hired worker will do, so the wage is not fixed—one dirham or two—so the ijarah wage is unknown, causing the ijarah to be fasid. Therefore, the ijarah is not valid, even if at the start of work it becomes known which wage applies. The principle is: if the wage is not known at the time of concluding the ijarah contract, the ijarah is fasid. 'Attar' means perfume seller; 'haddad' means blacksmith.
[1200] (45) Someone rented a house for one dirham per month, so the contract is valid for one month and fasid for the remaining months, unless the total months are specified as known. If someone rented a house and said: I will pay one dirham per month as rent. Then the ijarah is only for one month; the next month's ijarah is not done. The landlord can refuse to let it for the next month, and the tenant can refuse to take it. However, if the tenant starts living in the next month as well and the landlord says nothing, then a new ijarah takes place in the customary manner, like by indication (bay' al-ta'ati). Similarly, for as many months as they continue without refusal, each month a new ijarah occurs. And the day the landlord or tenant refuses to give or take the rent, the next ijarah ends. Yes, if he specifies all the months, then the ijarah is for as many months as he specifies. For example, if he specifies two years, it is for two years. If he does not specify all months, it is unknown how many months the ijarah is. But since he has spoken of one dirham per month, the minimum is one month's ijarah (2). There is an indication of this in an athar. From al-Thawri regarding a man who hires from a man to Mecca and guarantees the hired worker's expenses until he reaches, he said: No, unless he specifies known days and a known measure of food that he gives him each day (a) (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, باب الرجل یکترى على الشيء المحمول وهل يجوز الكراء ادیا خذ مثله منه؟ ج 8 ص 214 نمبر 14938). In this athar, it is that all days must be specified, and as long as all the hire is not specified, the ijarah is not valid. (3) In the hadith, it is that the sale of a heap of food whose amount is not known is prohibited. Similarly, if all months are not known, their ijarah is not valid. In the hadith: I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah that he forbade... Footnote: (a) al-Thawri said: A man hires from a man to Mecca and guarantees the hired worker's expenses until he arrives, he said: No, not unless he specifies known days and a known measure of food that he gives him each day.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage (45) discusses the ruling for renting a house at a rate of 'one dirham per month' without specifying the total number of months. The ruling is that the contract is valid only for the first month; for subsequent months, it is fasid unless the total months are made known. The reason is that the duration of the lease is unknown (majhool) at the time of contract, which creates uncertainty in the wage (since total rent depends on the number of months). However, the first month is valid because it is definite: the duration is one month, and the rent is one dirham. For subsequent months, the contract is not automatically extended; it requires tacit renewal month by month through conduct (similar to bay' al-ta'ati, a sale by indication). If the tenant continues to occupy and the landlord does not object, a new ijarah is formed each month on the same terms. Either party can refuse at the end of any month to continue. The text supports this with an athar from al-Thawri requiring days to be specified for a hire contract, analogizing to the hadith prohibiting sale of unspecified quantities. The core principle is that the ijarah contract must have a known duration and a known total wage (or at least a known wage per unit with known total units). If only the per-unit wage is known but not the number of units, the contract is limited to the first unit (one month) and then renewed tacitly. The mufta bihi position is that such a lease is valid for one month and then continues month-to-month unless terminated.

Key Terms
شهر (shahr): A calendar month; here used as the unit of time for rent without specifying the number of months
بیع تعاطی (bay' al-ta'ati): A sale or contract concluded by mutual exchange of goods/benefits without verbal offer and acceptance, by mutual conduct
اجارہ فاسد (ijarah fasidah): A defective ijarah that is not void but lacks a condition; in this context, it means the contract is not valid for the unspecified months unless renewed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling for a rental contract that says 'per month' without specifying the total number of months?
A) The contract is completely valid for as long as the tenant pays rent.
B) The contract is valid for the first month only; later months are fasid but can be renewed tacitly.
C) The contract is completely fasid because the total rent is unknown.
D) The contract is valid for one year after which it must be renewed.

Key Takeaway
A rental contract with a per-month rate but no fixed total term is valid only for the first month; continuation relies on tacit month-to-month renewal by both parties.

Ijarah — Hire and Lease

Renting a House Monthly: Valid Only for One Month
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute and evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a monthly rental without a fixed total, explain the dispute between Abu Hanifah and the Sahibayn, and apply the ruling to a similar ijarah case.

Core Idea
A monthly rental without a fixed total is valid only for the first month; uncertainty in duration invalidates future months.

Imagine renting a house for 'one dirham per month' without specifying how many months. Does the contract cover one month or all months until cancelled? This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri presents a clear intra-Hanafi dispute: Imam Abu Hanifah holds that only the first month is valid, while his two students (the Sahibayn) consider the entire contract invalid. Understanding this ruling is crucial for correctly structuring lease agreements in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Case and the Dispute
Read the scenario: a person rents a house at a rate of one dirham per month but does not specify the total months. Note that there are two positions: Abu Hanifah's and the Sahibayn's.
The lesson type is intra-Hanafi dispute.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifah's Position
Abu Hanifah rules the contract valid for the first month (since the month and rent are known) but invalid (fasid) for subsequent months.
The reasoning: the first month is a separate, known unit; future months are unknown, so invalid by analogy to the hadith on selling an unknown measure.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's Position
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold the entire contract invalid because at the time of contract the wage (ujrah) for the labor is unknown – the worker's task is undefined.
They argue that uncertainty in the rental period makes the wage majhul, voiding the whole contract.
4
Understand the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifah, the first month is binding; under the Sahibayn, no month is binding and the contract is void from the start.
This affects whether the tenant must vacate immediately or can stay for at least one month.
5
Apply the Mufta Bihi Ruling
The text presents Abu Hanifah's view as the primary ruling. Thus, the operative position for fatwa is that the contract is valid for the first month and subsequent months require a new agreement (even by conduct).
If the tenant stays with the owner's silence, a new ijarah is formed by ta'ati (mutual conduct).

Source Text

وقالا رحمهما الله الاجارة فاسدة . ۱۲۰۰ (۴۵) ومن استأجر دارا کل شهر بدرهم فالعقد صحيح في شهر واحد وفاسد في بقية الشهور الا ان يسمى جملة الشهور معلومة اس لئے اجارہ درست ہوگا۔ اور جو کام کرے گا اس قسم کی اجرت ملے گی۔ باقی کیا کام کرے گا اس کا تعین کام شروع کرتے وقت ہو جائے گا۔ انوں یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ دو کام الگ الگ ہوں اور ہر ایک کی اجرت معلوم ہو تو اجارہ درست ہے۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اجارہ کرتے وقت یہ پتہ نہیں ہے کہ کون سا کام اجیر کرے گا اس لئے کوان کی اجرت لازم ہوگی ، ایک درہم یا دو درہم یہ عقد اجارہ کے وقت طے نہیں ہے اس لئے اجارہ کی اجرت مجہول ہونے کی وجہ سے اجارہ فاسد ہو گیا۔ اس لئے اجارہ درست نہیں ہوا چاہے کام شروع کرتے وقت اس کا علم ہو جائے کہ کون سی اجرت ہوگی۔
اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ عقد اجارہ طے کرتے وقت اجرت کا علم نہ ہو تو اجارہ فاسد ہوگا۔
عطار : عطر بیچنے والا ۔ حداد : لوہاری کا کام کرنے والا۔
[۱۲۰۰] (۴۵) کسی نے گھر کرایہ پر لیا ہر ماہ ایک درہم کے بدلے تو عقد صحیح ہے ایک مہینے میں اور فاسد ہوگا باقی مہینوں میں مگر یہ کہ تمام معلوم
مہینے معن کر دئیے جائیں۔ کسی نے گھر کرایہ پر لیا اور یوں کہا کہ ہر ماہ ایک درہم کے بدلے اجرت دوں گا۔ تو ایک ہی مہینے کا اجارہ ہوا اگلے مہینے کا اجارہ نہیں ہوا۔ گھر والا اگلے مہینے اجرت پر دینے سے انکار کر دے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ اسی طرح کرایہ دار اگلے مہینے اجرت پر لینے سے انکار کر دے تو کر سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اگلے مہینہ بھی رہنا شروع کر دے اور گھر والا کچھ نہ کہے تو یہ از سر نو اجارہ ہوا جو معروف طریقے پر گویا کہ اشارے اشارے میں بیع تعاطی کے طور پر ہو گیا۔ اور اسی طرح جتنے مہینے بغیر انکار کے رہتے رہیں گے ہر ماہ نیا اجارہ ہوتا چلا جائے گا۔ اور جس دن گھر والا یا کرایہ دار اجرت دینے یا لینے سے انکار کر دے اسی دن اگلا اجارہ ختم ہو جائے گا۔ ہاں ! تمام مہینے متعین کر دے تو جتنے مہینے متعین کرے گا اتنے مہینے کی اجرت ہوگی۔ مثلا دو سال طے کیا تو دو سال کا اجارہ ہوگا۔
تمام مہینوں کو طے نہیں کیا تو کتنے مہینے کا اجارہ ہوگا یہ مجہول ہے۔ لیکن چونکہ ہر مہینہ ایک درہم کا بول چکا ہے اس لئے اقل درجہ ایک مہینہ کا اجارہ ہو جائے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن الشورى في رجل يكترى من رجل الى مكة ويضمن له الكرى نفقته الى ان يبلغ قال لا الا ان يوقت اياما معلومة وكيلا معلوما من الطعام يعطيه اياه كل يوم (الف) (مصنف عبدالرزاق، باب الرجل يكترى على الشيء المحمول وهل يجوز الكراء اديا خذ مثله منه؟ ج ثامن ص ۲۱۴ نمبر ۱۴۹۳۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ تمام دن متعین کر لئے جائیں اور ان کے تمام کرائے متعین نہ کر لئے جائیں تب تک اجارہ صحیح نہیں ہے (۳) حدیث میں ہے کہ ڈھیر کی مکمل مقدار معلوم نہ ہو تو اس کے بیچنے سے منع فرمایا ہے اس طرح تمام مہینے معلوم نہ ہوں تو ان کا اجارہ درست نہیں ہوگا حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت جابر بن عبد الله نهی حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ثوری نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی کسی آدمی سے مکہ تک کرایہ کے لئے لے اور مکہ تک پہنچنے تک اجیر کے نطقے کا ضامن ہوتو فرمایا یہ بھی نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ دن متعین کرے اور کھانے کا کیل معلوم ہو جو ہر دن دیگا ۔
And both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: the ijarah is invalid. (1200)(45) Whoever rents a house for each month for one dirham, the contract is valid for one month and invalid for the remaining months unless he specifies the total number of months as known. Therefore, the ijarah will be valid. Whatever work he does, he will receive that type of wage. As for what work he will do, its determination will occur at the time of starting work. This issue is based on the principle that if two tasks are separate and the wage for each is known, then the ijarah is valid. The two masters (Sahibayn) say: at the time of the ijarah contract, it is not known which work the laborer will do, so their wage becomes obligatory. One dirham or two dirhams – this is not fixed at the time of the ijarah contract, so due to the wage being unknown, the ijarah becomes invalid. Therefore the ijarah is not valid, even if at the time of starting work it becomes known what the wage will be. Principle: This issue is based on the principle that if at the time of concluding the ijarah contract the wage is not known, the ijarah will be invalid. 'Attar: perfume seller. Haddad: blacksmith. [1200](45) Someone rented a house for one dirham each month: the contract is valid for one month and invalid for the remaining months unless all the known months are specified. If someone rented a house and said, 'I will pay a rent of one dirham each month,' then only one month's ijarah occurred; the next month's ijarah did not occur. The owner can refuse to give it for rent the next month, and likewise the tenant can refuse to take it for rent the next month. However, if he begins staying in the next month and the owner says nothing, then this becomes a new ijarah, which according to the customary method, as it were by indication, happens like a mutual sale (bay' al-ta'ati). Similarly, as many months as they continue staying without objection, each month a new ijarah occurs. And on the day the owner or tenant refuses to give or take rent, from that day the next ijarah ends. Yes, if he specifies all the months, then the rent is for as many months as he specifies; for example, if he specifies two years, the ijarah will be for two years. If he did not specify all the months, how many months the ijarah covers is unknown. But since he has spoken of one dirham each month, at the very least one month's ijarah occurs. (2) There is an indication of this in the athar: From al-Thawri regarding a man who hires from a man to Mecca and guarantees for him the hire and his expenses until he arrives – he said: No, unless he specifies known days and a known measure of food which he gives him each day. (a) (Musannaf Abdurrazzaq, chapter: a man hires for something carried and whether it is permissible to hire a like for a like? vol.8 p.214 no.14938) In this athar, it is stated that unless all days are specified and all their hires are specified, the ijarah is not valid. (3) There is a hadith that selling a pile of dates whose full measure is unknown is prohibited. Similarly, if the total months are unknown, their ijarah is not valid. There is a hadith: I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah... prohibition. Footnote (a): Hadrat Thawri said: If a man takes from a man a hire to Mecca and guarantees the laborer's expenses until he arrives, he said: This is also not permissible unless he specifies the days and the measure of food to be given each day is known.
Source pages p. 205

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling on a specific ijarah case and a clear intra-Hanafi dispute. The ruling (45) from the matn states that if a person rents a house at a rate of one dirham per month but does not specify the total number of months, the contract is valid only for the first month and invalid for subsequent months. This is the position of Imam Abu Hanifah. The author then explains the reasoning: each month is treated as a separate contract, but since the total number of months is unknown, the contract for future months is invalid due to jahalah (uncertainty) of the rent period. However, for the first month, since the rent (one dirham) is known and the month is definite, the contract is valid. The Urdu commentary clarifies that if the tenant occupies the house in the second month with the owner's silent consent, a new ijarah is formed by conduct (ta'ati), similar to a sale by exchange without verbal contract. The two companions (Sahibayn – Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold a different view: they consider the entire contract invalid, even for the first month, because at the time of contract the exact work or rent obligation for future months is unknown, making the wage (ujrah) unknown, which invalidates the entire ijarah. The author then cites an athar from al-Thawri to support the principle that both the period and its wage must be known for validity. Additionally, a hadith prohibiting the sale of a pile of dates of unknown measure is used as an analogy (qiyas) here: just as a sale with unknown quantity is invalid, so is an ijarah with unknown duration. The key point is that the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifah) relies on the contract being valid for the first month as a separate, known unit, while the Sahibayn emphasize the overarching uncertainty. The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position according to the text seems to be that of Abu Hanifah, as the ruling is presented as the primary one.

Key Terms
اجارہ (ijarah): A contract for hire or lease of services or property for a specified wage.
صاحبین (sahibayn): Refers to the two major students of Abu Hanifah: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
بیع تعاطی (bay' al-ta'ati): A sale concluded by mutual exchange of goods without verbal offer and acceptance, based on customary practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person rents a house for 'each month for one dirham' without specifying the total number of months, what is the ruling on the first month?
A) The contract is valid for the first month
B) The contract is invalid for all months
C) The contract is valid for all months
D) The contract is valid only if the tenant pays for the first month in advance

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a monthly rental without a fixed term is valid only for the first month; subsequent months require a new agreement, and the Sahibayn's opposing view (entire contract invalid) is not the mufta bihi.

Staying an Hour in the Second Month Makes Ijarah Valid
Ruling on tacit renewal of ijarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a tenant's brief stay in the next month with the owner's silence makes the entire month's ijarah binding, and identify the proof from the athar.

Core Idea
One hour with silence = full month rent due.

This passage from a Hanafi text on ijarah deals with what happens when a tenant stays on after the rental period ends. Even a brief occupation with the owner's consent (by silence) creates a new binding contract for the next month. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle of contract formation by mutual conduct (ta'ati).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the tenant staying for even an hour in the second month. The ruling is that the ijarah contract for that entire month becomes valid and binding.
The contract is formed by mutual conduct, not explicit words.
2
Understand the condition
The owner must remain silent, implying consent. No explicit agreement is needed. The tenant's stay and owner's silence together constitute acceptance.
Silence in this context indicates satisfaction with the customary rate.
3
Derive the legal basis
The Hanafis analogize to bay' al-ta'ati (sale by conduct) and cite an athar from Hasan al-Basri to show that hiring by custom without explicit terms is valid.
The athar is considered proof for contract formation through customary indication.
4
Apply the rule
Determine that the full month's rent is owed and the owner cannot evict the tenant until the month ends.
The entire new month is treated as a valid ijarah period.
5
Note the evidence
The athar from Hasan al-Basri and Abdullah ibn Mirdas shows that a second hire was concluded without explicit negotiation, merely by riding and paying the customary hire.
The Hanafis use this as evidence that ijarah can be formed by conduct (ta'ati) when the customary rate is known.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۱۰۱ (۴۶) فان سكن ساعة من الشهر الثاني صح العقد فيه فلزمه ولم يكن للمؤجر ان يخرجه الى ان ينقضى الشهر المستأجر (۱۰۲) و کذلک حکم کل شهر يسكن في اوله يوما أو ساعة.
الموجر : اجرت پر دينے والا ۔ المستاجر : اجرت پر ديا ہوا گھر۔
[۱۲۰۱] (۴۶) پس اگر اگلے مہينے ميں ایک گھڑی ٹھہر گيا تو اس ميں عقد صحيح ہو جائے گا اور اس کو اجرت لازم ہوگی ۔ اور اجرت پر دينے والے کے لئے جائز نہيں ہے کہ اجير کو نکالے يہاں تک کہ اجرت پر ليا ہوا مہينہ ختم ہو جائے۔
ايک ماہ پورا ہونے کے بعد دوسرے مہينے ميں ایک گھڑی اس گھر ميں ٹھہر گيا اور گھر والا کچھ نہيں بولا تو يوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ بيچ تعاطی کی طرح اشاروں اشاروں ميں ہی اگلے ماہ کا اجارہ ہو گيا۔ گويا کہ دينے والا بھی اس اجرت پر راضی ہے اور لينے والا بھی اس اجرت پر راضی ہے تب ہی تو لينے والا اگلے ماہ ميں بھی اس گھر ميں ٹھہر رہا۔ اس لئے اجارہ درست ہوا۔ اور اس پورے مہينے ميں گھر والا کرايہ دار کو نہيں نکال سکتا۔ اثر ميں ہے۔ واکتری الحسـن مـن عبد الله بن مرداس حمارا فقال بكم؟ قال بدانقين فركبه ثم جاء مرة اخرى فقال الحمار الحمار فركبه ولم يشارطه فبعث اليه بنصف درهم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من اجری امر المصار علی ما يتعارفون بینھم فی البدع والاجارة ص۲۹۴ نمبر ۲۲۱۰) اس اثر ميں پہلی مرتبہ تو دو دانق گدھے کی اجرت طے کی لیکن دوسری مرتبہ آدھا درہم اجرت طے نہيں کی بلکہ حضرت حسن نے اجرت دیدی اور عبد اللہ بن مرد اس نے لے لی اور گويا کہ اشارے اشارے ميں اجرت طے ہو گئی۔ اس طرح جب دوسرے مہينے ميں کرايہ دار رہ گيا اور گھر والے نے کچھ نہيں کہا تو اشارے اشارے ميں اجرت طے ہو گئی۔ اس لئے اس پورے مہينے ميں کرايہ دار کو گھر سے نہيں نکال سکتا ۔
اصول بيچ تعاطی کی طرح اشارے اشارے ميں اجرت بھی طے ہوتی ہے۔
(101)(46) If he stays for an hour of the second month, the contract becomes valid in it and binding upon him, and it is not permissible for the lessor to evict him until the rented month expires. (102) And likewise the ruling for every month in which he stays at its beginning for a day or an hour. Al-Mu'jir: the one who gives on rent. Al-Musta'jir: the house given on rent. [1201](46) So if he stayed for an hour in the next month, the contract becomes valid in it and rent becomes binding on him. And it is not permissible for the lessor to evict the lessee until the rented month ends. After one month is complete, if he stayed for an hour in the next month and the owner said nothing, then it will be understood that by mutual indication, like a mutual sale, the next month's ijarah occurred. As if the lessor is pleased with this rent and the lessee is also pleased with it, for that reason the lessee remained in the house in the next month. Therefore the ijarah is valid, and for the whole month the owner cannot evict the tenant. There is an athar: Hasan hired a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mirdas; he asked, 'How much?' He said, 'Two daniqs.' He rode it, then came another time and said, 'The donkey! The donkey!' He rode it without bargaining, so he sent him half a dirham. (b) (Sahih al-Bukhari, chapter: Whoever conducts his affairs based on what is customary among them in leasing and ijarah, p.294 no.2210) In this athar, the first time the rent of the donkey was fixed at two daniqs, but the second time the half dirham rent was not fixed; rather Hadrat Hasan gave the rent and Abdullah ibn Mirdas took it, and thus by mutual indication the rent was fixed. Similarly, when the tenant stayed in the second month and the owner said nothing, the rent was fixed by mutual indication. Therefore, for the whole month, the owner cannot evict the tenant from the house. Principle: Just like in mutual sale (bay' al-ta'ati), by mutual indication rent is also fixed.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage provides a secondary ruling within the same ijarah case. The matn (101) states that if the tenant stays for even an hour in the second month, the contract for that entire month becomes valid and binding, preventing the lessor from evicting him until the month ends. The ruling is extended to every month where the tenant stays at its beginning for a day or an hour (102). The Urdu commentary explains the reasoning: such brief occupation with the owner's silence constitutes a new ijarah contract by conduct (ta'ati), analogous to a sale without verbal exchange. An athar from Hasan al-Basri and Abdullah ibn Mirdas is cited to show that customary mutual indication establishes the lease. Thus, the second month's ijarah is valid for the full month, and the owner cannot evict. This demonstrates the Hanafi principle that contracts can be formed through customary indication, not just explicit words.

Key Terms
موجر (mu'jir): The person who gives property on rent (lessor).
مستأجر (musta'jir): The person who takes property on rent (lessee).
اجیر (ajir): The person who provides service or labor (the tenant in this context is like an ajir using the property).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a tenant stays in the rented house for one hour on the first day of the second month without a new explicit agreement, and the owner says nothing, what is the ruling?
A) The tenant must leave immediately
B) The contract for the second month becomes valid and binding for the full month
C) The tenant must negotiate a new rent
D) The owner can evict the tenant at any time

Key Takeaway
Silent acceptance of brief occupation creates a binding ijarah for the full period.

Same Ruling for Any Month with Initial Stay
Extension of renewal ruling to all months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on monthly ijarah renewal and identify the condition of initial stay at the start of the month that triggers a new contract.

Core Idea
A brief stay at the start of any month renews the ijarah by mutual indication.

This short passage builds on the previous ruling (issue 46) which established that a tenant's stay at the beginning of the second month, without the owner's objection, forms a new ijarah contract. Here, that ruling is extended to every subsequent month. The legal mechanism remains the same: a brief occupancy at the month's start, combined with silent consent, is sufficient to renew the tenancy. This is a key procedural rule in Hanafi ijarah for monthly rentals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its trigger
The act is the renewal of an ijarah contract for a new month. The trigger is the tenant's stay at the beginning of that month – even for just a day or an hour.
The stay must occur at the very start of the month, not at the end or middle.
2
Recognize the condition
The condition for renewal is that the tenant actually resides at the start of the month. The owner's silence in response is interpreted as consent (mutual indication).
If the owner explicitly objects, no renewal occurs.
3
Understand the legal mechanism
The renewal is not by a new explicit contract but by mutual indication (dalalat al-hal) – the tenant's action and the owner's silence together indicate a new agreement.
Hanafi fiqh accepts implicit consent in ongoing relationships.
4
Apply the scope of the ruling
This rule applies to every month after the first, not just the second. The text says 'wa kaza hukmu kulli shahrin' – the same ruling for every month.
The first month is governed by the original contract; subsequent months are renewed under this rule.
5
Recall the evidence
The author refers back to the hadith and reasoning (qiyas) that were cited for the second month in the previous issue. The same proofs apply here.
The earlier evidence is not repeated but is considered established.

اگلے ہر ماہ میں جب مہینے کے شروع میں ایک دن یا ایک گھڑی ٹھہر جائے تو گھر والے کی رضامندی سمجھی جائے گی اور اشارے اشارے میں اگلے مہینے کی اجرت طے ہو جائے گی۔ حدیث اور وجہ گزر گئے۔
(47) And likewise is the ruling for every month: if he stays at its beginning for a day or an hour. In each next month, when he stays for a day or an hour at the beginning of the month, the owner's consent will be assumed and the rent for the next month will be fixed by mutual indication. The hadith and reasoning have passed.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This short passage simply reiterates that the ruling stated in issue (46) applies to every month following the first, not just the second month. The legal reasoning is the same: a brief stay at the start of any month, without objection from the owner, forms a new ijarah contract by mutual indication. The reference to 'the hadith and reasoning have passed' means the evidence cited earlier (the athar and analogy) applies here as well. This is an important procedural point for monthly tenancy agreements; each month's renewal is conditional on actual occupancy with silent consent.

Key Terms
اشارے اشارے (ishārah ishārah): Mutual indication: a legal mechanism where actions and silence imply a contract without explicit words.
رضامندی (razāmandī): Consent; in this context, the owner's silent approval is assumed from the fact he did not object.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi ijarah, a brief stay at the start of any month, without the owner's objection, renews the rental contract for that month by mutual indication.

Implicit Renewal of Lease by Staying Past Term
Ruling and proof for lease renewal by indication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a tenant stays past the lease term without explicit agreement and explain the legal basis using bay' al-ta'ati and implied consent.

Core Idea
Staying an hour into the next month with landlord's silence creates a binding lease for the entire month by custom.

This lesson addresses a common practical scenario: a tenant remains in a rented property after the lease expires. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling based on implied consent (qarinah) and custom ('urf). We will see how the principle of bay' al-ta'ati applies to ijarah and the evidence from hadith and athar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The text presents: if a tenant stays even an hour in the second month, the lease is valid and binding for the entire month. Identify the act (staying past term) and the ruling (valid lease for full month).
The ruling applies regardless of how short the initial stay is.
2
Understand the basis: implied consent via bay' al-ta'ati
The author compares this to sale by mutual action (bay' al-ta'ati) where no verbal offer/acceptance is needed; custom suffices. Here, the landlord's silence and tenant's continued occupancy indicate mutual agreement.
This is a form of 'urf (custom) that the Hanafi school accepts.
3
Examine the primary dalil: hadith on unknown measure
The hadith prohibits selling a heap of dates when the measure is unknown. The text uses this to show that if the months of a lease were unknown, the contract would be invalid. But here, the month becomes known by the tenant's stay and landlord's consent.
The analogy is that the duration is effectively specified by the parties' actions.
4
Examine the supporting athar: Hasan al-Basri's donkey rental
The athar shows that when Hasan rented a donkey a second time without explicit terms, payment was made and accepted, establishing that mutual indication creates a valid hire.
This supports the principle that silence and action can form a contract.
5
Apply the ruling and note the consequence
Because the lease is valid for the full month, the landlord cannot evict the tenant until that month ends, and the tenant must pay rent for the full month.
The same rule applies to any subsequent month where the tenant stays on the first day or hour.

رسول الله لا لا اله عن بيع الصبرة من التمر لا يعلم مكيلها بالكيل المسمى من التمر (الف) (مسلم شریف، باب تحریم بیع صبرة التمر المجهولة القدر تمرج ثاني ص 4 نمبر 1530) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ڈھیر کی تمام مقدار معلوم نہ ہوتو بیچنا صیح نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس کی قیمت بھی مجہول ہوگی ۔ اسی طرح تمام مہینے معلوم نہیں ہوں تو ان کا اجارہ بیچ نہیں ہوگا۔ (1201) (46) پس اگر اگلے مہینے میں ایک گھڑی ٹھہبر گیا تو اس میں عقد صحیح ہو جائے گا اور اس کو اجرت لازم ہوگی ۔ اور اجرت پر دینے والے کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ اجیر کو نکالے یہاں تک کہ اجرت پر لیا ہوا مہینہ ختم ہو جائے۔
ایک ماہ پورا ہونے کے بعد دوسرے مہینے میں ایک گھڑی اس گھر میں ٹھہر گیا اور گھر والا کچھ نہیں بولا تو یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ بیع تعاطی کی طرح اشاروں اشاروں میں ہی اگلے ماہ کا اجارہ ہو گیا۔ گویا کہ دینے والا بھی اس اجرت پر راضی ہے اور لینے والا بھی اس اجرت پر راضی ہے تب ہی تو لینے والا اگلے ماہ میں بھی اس گھر میں ظہرارہا۔ اس لئے اجارہ درست ہوا۔ اور اس پورے مہینے میں گھر والا کرایہ دار کو نہیں نکال سکتا۔ اثر میں ہے۔ واکتری الحسـن مـن عبد الله بن مرداس حمارا فقال بكم؟ قال بدانقين فركبه ثم جاء مرة اخرى فقال الحمار الحمار فركبه ولم يشارطه فبعث اليه بنصف درهم (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب من اجری امر المصار علی ما يتعارفون بینھم فی البدع والاجارة ص294 نمبر 2210) اس اثر میں پہلی مرتبہ تو دو دانق گدھے کی اجرت طے کی لیکن دوسری مرتبہ آدھا درہم اجرت طے نہیں کی بلکہ حضرت حسن نے اجرت دیدی اور عبد اللہ بن مرد اس نے لے لی اور گویا کہ اشارے اشارے میں اجرت طے ہو گئی۔ اس طرح جب دوسرے مہینے میں کرایہ دار رہ گیا اور گھر والے نے کچھ نہیں کہا تو اشارے اشارے میں اجرت طے ہو گئی۔ اس لئے اس پورے مہینے میں کرایہ دار کو گھر سے نہیں نکال سکتا ۔
اصول بیچ تعاطی کی طرح اشارے اشارے میں اجرت بھی طے ہوتی ہے۔
الموجر : اجرت پر دینے والا ۔ المستاجر : اجرت پر دیا ہوا گھر۔

اگلے ہر ماہ میں جب مہینے کے شروع میں ایک دن یا ایک گھڑی ٹھہر جائے تو گھر والے کی رضامندی سمجھی جائے گی اور اشارے اشارے میں اگلے مہینے کی اجرت طے ہو جائے گی۔ حدیث اور وجہ گزر گئے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے کھجور کے اس ڈھیر سے بیچنے سے منع فرمایا جس کا متعین کیل معلوم نہ ہو۔ (ب) حضرت حسن نے عبد اللہ بن مرداس سے گدھا کرایہ پر لیا اور پوچھا کتنا کرایہ ہے؟ کہا دو دانق پس اس پر سوار ہوئے پھر دوسری مرتبہ آئے اور کہا گدھا چاہئے ۔ پس اس پر سوار ہوئے اور کرائے کی شرط نہیں کی پھر اس کو آدھا در ہم بھیج دیا۔
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 2, p.201, Book of Ijarah. [101 (46) If he stays an hour of the second month, the contract becomes valid and binding, and the lessor cannot evict him until the hired month ends. (102) And likewise is the ruling for every month in which he stays on its first day or hour. The Messenger of Allah forbade the sale of a heap of dates whose measure is not known for a specified measure of dates. (Muslim, chapter on prohibition of selling a heap of dates of unknown measure, no. 1530) This hadith states that if the total amount of a heap is unknown, selling it is not correct because its price would be unknown. Similarly, if the whole months are unknown, their ijarah would not be valid. (1201) (46) So if he stays for an hour in the next month, the contract becomes valid and rent is binding. And it is not permissible for the lessor to evict the tenant until the hired month ends. After one month is complete, if he stays an hour in the second month and the landlord says nothing, then it is understood that like bay' al-ta'ati (sale by mutual action), the lease for the next month is concluded by mutual indication. That is, both the lessor and the tenant are satisfied with that rent, because otherwise the tenant would not remain in the house. Therefore, the lease is valid, and the landlord cannot evict the tenant for the entire month. There is an athar: Hasan rented a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mirdas. He asked: How much? He said: Two daniqs. He rode it, then came another time and said: The donkey, the donkey. He rode it without stipulating, then sent him half a dirham. (Bukhari, chapter on managing affairs according to custom in contracts and leases, no. 2210) In this athar, the first time the hire was fixed as two daniqs, but the second time half a dirham was not fixed; rather, Hasan gave the hire, and Abdullah ibn Mirdas took it, so it is as if the hire was fixed by indication. Similarly, when the tenant stayed in the second month and the landlord said nothing, the hire was fixed by indication. Therefore, the tenant cannot be evicted from the house for the full month. The principle: Just as sale by mutual action, hire is also fixed by indication. Al-mu'jir: the one giving on hire. Al-mustajir: the one taking on hire. [1202] (47) And the same applies to every month: if he stays on its beginning for a day or an hour, then the landlord's consent is understood and by indication the hire for the next month is fixed. The hadith and evidence have already passed. Footnote: (a) He forbade selling a heap of dates whose specific measure is not known. (b) Hasan rented a donkey from Abdullah ibn Mardas and asked how much the hire; he said two daniqs, so he rode it; then he came another time and said: I need the donkey, so he rode it without stipulating the hire, then sent him half a dirham.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Ijarah concerning the situation where a tenant remains in the leased property beyond the agreed term. The key ruling: if the tenant stays for even an hour in the next month, the lease contract is considered valid for that entire month, and the landlord cannot evict him until that month expires. The author provides proof by analogy to a hadith that prohibits selling a heap of dates when the quantity is unknown, inferring that if the months are not specified, the lease would be invalid due to ignorance. However, in this case, the tenant's act of staying with the landlord's implicit consent creates a new lease by 'urf (custom) and mutual indication (bay' al-ta'ati). This is supported by an athar from Hasan al-Basri concerning a donkey rental where the second hire was not explicitly agreed but was accepted by both parties. The principle is established that if the landlord does not object when the tenant stays, it constitutes consent and a new lease for the month. The passage also generalizes this rule to any month where the tenant stays on its first day or hour.

Key Terms
اجازہ (ijarah): Lease or hire contract.
موجر (mu'jir): The lessor or hirer.
مستاجر (musta'jir): The lessee or hiree.
بیع تعاطی (bay' al-ta'ati): Sale by mutual action without verbal offer and acceptance, relied upon by custom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a tenant staying past the lease term with the landlord's silence creates a valid lease for the entire ensuing month based on custom and mutual indication.

beginner
6 min
Tenant Stays Beyond Fixed Term: Rent Only for Agreed Period
Ruling that staying beyond the lease term is considered borrowing (ariyah), not a new lease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a tenant stays beyond the fixed lease term and explain why the extra period is considered ariyah (borrowing) rather than a new lease.

Core Idea
Rent is only due for the agreed term; staying beyond is ariyah, not a lease.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario from the Book of Ijarah: a tenant rents a house for one month but stays for two. The ruling clarifies what rent is owed. The key principle is that the lease automatically ends at the fixed term, and any continued occupancy is by the owner's permission as a gratuitous loan (ariyah). This has important implications for both landlords and tenants, ensuring that no rent is due beyond the agreed period unless a new contract is formed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Consider the act: renting a house for one month but staying two. The ruling states that only the first month's rent is due, and nothing for the second month.
The second month is not considered a lease extension.
2
Locate the governing principle
The author explains that after the lease term ends, any use of the property is legally treated as ariyah (gratuitous loan) because the original contract has expired.
Ariyah is a free loan of use, not a rental.
3
Apply the principle to the extra month
Since the second month falls after the fixed term, the tenant's occupancy is by the owner's tacit permission as ariyah, so no rent is legally due.
The tenant is not liable for rent for the second month.
4
Distinguish from the case without a fixed term
If the lease term is not fixed (as in a previous case), silence at the start of each month may imply renewal, making rent due each month. Here, the fixed term makes the end explicit.
Fixed term vs. indefinite term changes the ruling.
5
Note the ethical recommendation
Although not obligatory, the tenant is encouraged to voluntarily pay for the extra month as an act of ihsan (excellence).
This is a moral, not legal, obligation.

كتاب الاجارة
1203 (48) واذا استأجر دارا شهرا بدرهم فسکن شهرین فعليه اجرة الشهر الاول ولا شيء عليه من الشهر الثاني (1203) (38) اگر ایک گھر کو ایک مہینے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا ایک درہم کے بدلے، پھر اس میں دو مینے ٹھہرا تو اجیر پر پہلے مہینے کی اجرت ہے اور اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہے دوسرے مہینے کی۔
ایک گھر صرف ایک ماہ کے لئے ایک درہم کے بدلے اجرت پر لیا اور دو مہینے رہ گیا تو ایک ہی مہینے کی اجرت لازم ہوگی ، دوسرے مہینے کی اجرت لازم نہیں ہوگی۔
جب صرف ایک مہینے کی اجرت طے ہوئی تو ایک مہینے کے بعد اجارہ ختم ہو گیا۔ اب جو کرایہ دار رہا وہ اجرت کے طور پر نہیں بلکہ عاریت
کے طور پر رہا ہے اور مالک کی جانب سے اجازت کی وجہ سے مفت رہا اس لئے دوسرے مہینے کی اجرت اس پر لازم نہیں ہوگی ۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ مدت اجرت ختم ہونے کے بعد کرایہ دار جو کچھ استعمال کرے گا وہ عاریت کے طور گواجرت کے طور پر نہیں۔ کیونکہ اجارہ تو مستقل طور پر طے کرنے کے بعد منعقد ہوتا ہے ورنہ نہیں۔ یہ اس صورت میں ہے جب مدت اجرت طے ہو چکی ہو۔ لیکن مدت اجرت طے نہ ہوئی ہو تو مسئلہ نمبر 46 کی طرح ہر ماہ کے شروع میں اشارے اشارے میں اجارہ منعقد ہوتا رہے گا۔ اور ہر ماہ کی اجرت لازم ہوتی رہے گی۔ اس عاریت کی صورت میں بھی اجیر کو دوسرے مہینے کی اجرت اپنی خوشی سے پیش کر دینا چاہئے ۔ هل جزاء الاحسان الا عاریت کی صورت میں بھی اجر کو مہینے کی اپنی خوشی سے کردینا چاہئے۔
الاحسان.
Al-Sharh al-Thamiri, Part 2, p.202, Book of Ijarah. 1203 (48) If he rents a house for a month for a dirham and stays two months, then he owes the rent of the first month and nothing for the second month. (1203) (38) If a house is rented for one month for one dirham, then he stays two months, the tenant owes the first month's rent and nothing from the second month. A house rented for only one month for one dirham and he stays two months, only the first month's rent is due, not the second month's rent. When only one month's rent was fixed, after one month the lease ended. Now whatever stay the tenant does, it is not as a lease but as borrowing (ariyah) and due to the owner's permission, it was free. So the second month's rent is not due. This ruling is based on the principle that after the lease term ends, whatever use the tenant makes is considered borrowing, not lease. Because lease is only contracted by explicit agreement. This applies when the lease term is fixed. But if the lease term is not fixed, then like question 46, at the beginning of each month, the lease is concluded by indication and each month's rent becomes due. Even in this case of borrowing, it is recommended that the tenant voluntarily pay the second month's rent. 'Is the reward of ihsan anything but ihsan?' So even in borrowing, he should voluntarily pay the month's rent. Ihsan.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling on a case where a tenant rents a house for a fixed period (one month) but stays for two months. The key ruling: the tenant only owes rent for the first month; the second month is considered ariyah (gratuitous loan) because the lease automatically ended after the first month. The author distinguishes this from the previous case (46) where the term was not fixed. Here, the fixed term expired, so continued occupancy is by the owner's tacit permission as a favor, not as a renewed lease. The tenant is not legally obliged to pay for the second month, but it is recommended to pay voluntarily as an act of ihsan. The principle is that after the lease term, any use is ariyah unless a new lease is explicitly or implicitly agreed (as in case 46 where silence at the start of a new month implies renewal).

Key Terms
عاریة (ariyah): Gratuitous loan of property for use.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person rents a house for one month for $500 and stays for two months, what rent is due?
A) $1000 for two months
B) $500 for the first month only
C) $500 for the second month only
D) Nothing at all

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, once a lease term ends, continued occupancy is a gratuitous loan, not a new lease, so no additional rent is owed.

Validity of Annual Lease Without Specifying Monthly Rent
Ruling that a lease with lump sum annual rent is valid even without monthly breakdown.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a lease with a lump sum annual rent and explain why specifying monthly installments is not required.

Core Idea
A lease is valid if total period and total rent are known; monthly breakdown is unnecessary.

When entering a lease, both parties must agree on the essential terms: the duration and the total rent. But do you need to specify how much is due each month? In this lesson, we examine a clear Hanafi ruling that when the total is fixed, the monthly portion is implicitly known and the contract is valid. We also look at a proof from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, confirming the permissibility of lump-sum contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the first part of the passage: 'If he rents a house for a year for ten dirhams, it is valid...' The act is a lease (ijara) for a fixed period with a known total rent. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) even without specifying monthly installments.
2
Understand the reason for validity
The passage explains: because the total period is specified and the total rent is specified, there is no ignorance (gharar) about the essential terms. Note the condition: both total duration and total consideration must be known.
Gharar in the total rent or period would invalidate the contract.
3
Examine the evidence from the Salaf
The author cites the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who sold the fruit of a deceased debtor's land for two years without specifying monthly installments. This is analogous (qiyas) to a lease for a lump sum. Identify the dalil: a narration from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
The dalil is a qawl sahabi (opinion of a Companion), which is considered a valid proof in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Recall the underlying principle
The passage states: 'when the annual rent is specified, there is no need to specify the monthly installment.' This is a general principle: fixing the total implicitly determines the parts. The same principle applies to other contracts where the total is known.
This principle helps avoid unnecessary formalism in contracts.

Source Text

If he rents a house for a year for ten dirhams, it is valid even if he does not specify the installment for each month of the rent. 1204 (49) If a house is taken on rent for one year for ten dirhams, it is permissible even if the monthly installment of the rent is not specified. A man took a house on rent for a full year for ten dirhams and did not state how much each month would be, it is permissible. Because the total period is specified and the total rent is specified, so no ignorance remains. Therefore it is permissible. Even if the daily or monthly installment is not specified, because after the total period is fixed, there is no need. And if someone wants to know, he can calculate and find the monthly installment: each month would be approximately eighty-three paise. The principle: when the annual rent is specified, there is no need to specify the monthly installment; the lease is valid. There is evidence in this athar: Usaid ibn Hudair died and had a debt, so Umar sold the fruit of his land for two years. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, vol.5, p.13, no.23250) In this athar, fruit was sold for two years without specifying the monthly installment. Qist: the estimation and portion of rent each month. Footnote: (a) Usaid ibn Hudair passed away with debt, so Umar sold the fruit of his land for two years.

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling that a lease for a fixed period (one year) with a fixed total rent (ten dirhams) is valid even if the breakdown into monthly installments is not explicitly stated. The reason is that the essential elements (duration and total consideration) are known, so there is no gharar (uncertainty). The author provides evidence from the practice of Umar ibn al-Khattab, who sold the fruit of a deceased debtor's land for two years without specifying monthly amounts, which is analogous to a lease. The principle is that when the total is fixed, the parts are implicitly known and calculable. Therefore, the lease is valid.

Key Terms
قسط (qist): Installment; the portion of rent for each month.

Key Takeaway
A lease is valid if the total duration and total rent are fixed; the monthly breakdown is not required.

Extra Stay After Rental Term Ends: Ijarah and 'Ariyah
Ruling on extra stay after rental term ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on extra stay after a fixed-term rental and distinguish between ijarah and 'ariyah.

Core Idea
Once the fixed rental term ends, the property reverts to free use ('ariyah), not renewed rent.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi ruling from the Book of Ijarah. When a tenant stays beyond the agreed term with the owner's permission, the contract does not automatically renew; instead, the extra period is considered a loan for use ('ariyah). This principle has practical implications for tenancies and temporary stays.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fixed term and rent
The contract is for a specific month for a specific rent. Note that the term is fixed.
Fixed-term ijarah is a condition for this ruling.
2
Recognise termination of ijarah at end of term
When the fixed term expires, the ijarah contract terminates automatically. It does not renew by silence or continued use.
This is a key Hanafi position.
3
Classify the extra stay based on permission
If the owner permits the tenant to stay (expressly or by silence with knowledge), the extra stay is considered 'ariyah (gratuitous loan). Without permission, it would be ghasb (usurpation).
Permission is the decisive factor.
4
Determine the ruling: no additional rent
Since the extra stay is 'ariyah, not ijarah, no rent is due for the extra period. The tenant is only liable for the contracted term.
Mufta bihi: no rent due.
5
Understand the voluntary gift recommendation
The tenant is encouraged to give a voluntary gift (not rent) to the owner for the extra stay, based on the verse 'Is there any reward for goodness other than goodness?' (Quran 55:60).
This is not obligatory, but commendable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الاجارة
۱۲۰۳ (۴۸) واذا استأجر دارا شهرا بدرهم فسکن شهرین فعليه اجرة الشهر الاول ولا شيء عليه من الشهر الثاني
(۱۲۰۳) (۳۸) اگر ایک گھر کو ایک مہینے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا ایک درہم کے بدلے، پھر اس میں دو مینے ٹھہرا تو اجیر پر پہلے مہینے کی اجرت ہے اور اس پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہے دوسرے مہینے کی۔
ایک گھر صرف ایک ماہ کے لئے ایک درہم کے بدلے اجرت پر لیا اور دو مہینے رہ گیا تو ایک ہی مہینے کی اجرت لازم ہوگی ، دوسرے مہینے کی اجرت لازم نہیں ہوگی۔

الاحسان.
If a person hires a house for a month for one dirham, then stays for two months, he is liable for the rent of the first month, and nothing is due from him for the second month.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Book of Ijarah (hire/lease). The Arabic matn states that when a person hires a house for one month for a dirham and then stays for two months, he only owes the rent for the first month; no rent is due for the second month. The Urdu commentary explains the underlying principle: once the contracted term ends, the ijarah contract is terminated. The tenant's continued use of the property is not ijarah but 'ariyah (temporary loan with permission). Since the landlord's permission allows free use, no rent is owed for the additional month. However, the commentary notes that if the rental term was not fixed (i.e., the tenancy was indefinite), the ijarah would renew month-by-month as per the earlier ruling (mas'alah 46). The commentary also recommends that the tenant should voluntarily offer a gift (not rent) for the extra month, citing the verse 'Is there any reward for goodness other than goodness?' (Quran 55:60, implied). The principle is that once the fixed term ends, the property is not automatically rented; it reverts to the owner's control. The key distinction: if the term is fixed, extra stay is 'ariyah; if not fixed, it is a series of consecutive ijarah contracts.

Key Terms
عاریت ('ariyah): Temporary loan or gratuitous permission to use something without payment of rent.
اجارہ (ijarah): Contract of hire/lease for fixed term and rent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person hires a house for one month and stays for two months, what is the Hanafi ruling regarding the second month's rent?
A) He must pay rent for the second month as well.
B) He owes no rent for the second month because the ijarah ended and the use became 'ariyah.
C) He must pay double rent for the second month.
D) The second month is considered a separate ijarah contract and he must pay the same rent.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a fixed-term ijarah ends at term; extra stay with permission is a loan, not rent.

Hiring a House with a Lump-Sum Rent: Validity Without Monthly Breakdown
Ruling on ijarah with total period and total rent determined but without monthly breakdown

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of an ijarah contract when the total period and total rent are specified but monthly installments are not, and explain the evidence from the practice of Caliph Umar (RA).

Core Idea
A lease is valid if the total term and total rent are fixed; monthly breakdown is not a condition.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in ijarah (hiring or leasing): a person rents a house for a full year for a lump sum, without stating how much is due each month. The Hanafi school declares such a contract valid, based on the principle that certainty (ma'lum) in the essential terms suffices. We'll explore the ruling, its rationale, and the evidence from the practice of Caliph Umar (RA).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is an ijarah (hire/lease) contract for a house for one year with a total rent of ten dirhams. The ruling is that it is valid (ja'iz).
2
Understand the conditions for validity
For an ijarah to be valid, the lease period and the total rent must be known. The monthly breakdown is not a condition; its omission does not create harmful uncertainty (jahalah).
The total period and total rent are both specified, so no jahalah remains.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
The commentary cites an athar: Caliph Umar (RA) sold the fruits of a garden for two years without specifying monthly installments, to settle a debt. This shows that a lump-sum agreement over a period is valid by analogy.
The dalil is the practice of a Companion (athar), which is considered evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Apply the principle to similar cases
The principle extends to any lease where the total rent and total period are fixed. If someone wants to know the monthly amount, it can be calculated by division.
The legal maxim: 'If the annual rent is fixed, specifying the monthly installment is not required.'
5
Address common misconceptions
Some think that monthly rent must be explicitly stated. Hanafi law holds that only the overall terms need to be known; the breakdown is secondary.
This facilitates transactions and reduces unnecessary formalities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت اسید بن حضیر کا انتقال ہو ۔ ان پر قرض تھا تو حضرت عمر نے اس کی زمین کے پھل دو سال کے لئے بیچ دیا۔
If a person hires a house for a year for ten dirhams, it is permissible even if he did not specify the installment for each month of the rent.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on ijarah. The Arabic matn states that hiring a house for a year for ten dirhams is valid even without specifying how much is due each month. The Urdu commentary explains the reasoning: the total period (one year) and total rent (ten dirhams) are both fixed, so there is no uncertainty (jahalah) that invalidates the contract. The monthly breakdown can be calculated by simply dividing (approximately 0.833 dirham per month, which in Indian currency is about 83 paise). The commentary cites a historical precedent from the practice of Caliph Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): he sold the fruits of a garden for two years (similar to a lease) without specifying monthly installments, to pay off the debts of Usayd ibn Hudayr. This shows that it is permissible to have a lump-sum rental for a fixed period. The key principle: as long as the overall term and total consideration are defined, the contract is valid; daily or monthly apportionment is not a condition.

Key Terms
قسط (qist): Installment or portion of rent due for a specific period (e.g., monthly).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, is it valid to hire a house for one year for a lump sum of ten dirhams without stating the monthly rent?
A) No, because the monthly rent must be specified.
B) Yes, it is valid because the total period and total rent are known.
C) Yes, but only if both parties agree verbally.
D) No, because the rent cannot be in a lump sum for more than one month.

Key Takeaway
A lease contract is valid in Hanafi law if the total period and total rent are known; monthly installments need not be specified.

Prohibition of Wages for Stud Service (عسب الفحل)
Ruling with dalil and ta'lil for prohibition of stud fees

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on taking wages for stud service, cite the hadith evidence, and explain the underlying principle of gharar.

Core Idea
Taking wages for animal stud service is haram due to prophetic prohibition and uncertainty of benefit.

In this lesson, we examine a specific transaction prohibited in the Hanafi school: charging a fee for allowing a male animal to mate with a female. This ruling is derived from an explicit hadith and reinforced by the principle of gharar (uncertainty). The source passage provides the ruling, textual evidence, and rational explanation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is taking wages for stud service (عسب الفحل). The ruling is impermissible (haram).
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Umar: 'نهى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم عن عسب الفحل' (the Prophet forbade the stud fee).
Reported in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition (nahy) indicates the act is haram. In Hanafi usul, a prohibition without qualifying context indicates tahrim.
4
Understand the underlying 'illa
The uncertainty of pregnancy (gharar) makes the payment a jahalah (unknown benefit). This falls under prohibited gharar in transactions.
5
Note the exception
If the owner of the male animal receives a gift voluntarily (not conditioned on service), it is permissible.
The gift is not considered a wage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۱۲۰۶] (۵۱) اور نہیں جائز ہے نر کو مادہ پر کو دانے کی اجرت لینا۔ سانڈ کو مادہ سے جفتی کروانے کی اجرت لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔
حدیث میں اس کی اجرت لینے سے منع فرمایا ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال نهى النبي الاله لال له عن عسب الفحل (ج) ( بخاری شریف ب عسب المحل ص ۳۰۵ نمبر ۲۲۸۴ر مسلم شریف، باب تحریم بیع فضل الماء... تحریم بیع ضراب النحل ص ۸۱ نمبر ۱۵۲۵ر ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی عسب الفحل ص ۱۳۰ نمبر ۳۴۲۹) اس حدیث میں جفتی کرانے کی اجرت لینے سے منع فرمایا ہے (۲) جفتی سے حمل ٹھہرے گا یا نہیں کوئی یقینی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے نفع ہونا کوئی یقینی نہیں ہوا اس لئے بھی نفع مجہول رہا اس لئے بھی اجرت لینا جائز نہین (۳) جفتی کی اجرت معاشرے کے اعتبار سے بھی ناپسندیدہ ہے۔ اونٹ والے کو عزت و احترام کے لئے کچھ دیدے تو اس کی گنجائش ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن انس بن مالک ان رجلا من
حاشیہ : (ج) حضور نے سانڈ کو دانے کی اجرت سے منع فرمایا۔
It is not permissible to take wages for the covering of a female by a male animal. Taking wages for the copulation of a bull is not permissible.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage addresses the prohibition of taking payment for the stud service of animals (casp al-fahl). The Urdu commentary begins by stating the ruling: it is not permissible to take wages for allowing a male animal to cover a female. It then provides evidence: a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade the wages for the stud male. The hadith is reported in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud. The commentary then gives three reasons: (1) The explicit prohibition in the hadith. (2) The uncertainty (gharar) involved: whether pregnancy will occur is not certain, so the benefit is uncertain, making the payment akin to gambling. (3) The act is socially undesirable. However, the commentary notes an exception: if the owner of the male animal is given a gift as a gesture of honor (not as a condition for the service), it is permissible. The principle: any transaction involving uncertain benefit (jahalah) is invalid in Hanafi fiqh, and this is reflected in the prohibition of stud fees.

Key Terms
عسب الفحل (casp al-fahl): The fee given for the stud service of a male animal (e.g., a bull or camel) to cover a female.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on taking wages for allowing a male animal to mate with a female (stud service)?
A) Permissible, because it is a service.
B) Permissible only if the payment is made as a gift.
C) Not permissible (haram) due to prophetic prohibition and uncertainty of benefit.
D) Makruh tanzihi, but not haram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits stud fees due to explicit hadith and gharar; only voluntary gifts without condition are allowed.

Ruling on Wages for Hammam and Cupping
States permissibility of wages for bathhouse and cupping with hadith evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that taking wages for hammam and cupping is permissible (ja'iz) in the Hanafi school and identify the prophetic proofs from the hadith of Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Prophet's example makes hammam and cupping wages permissible despite impurity concerns.

This lesson examines the permissibility of wages for two services often associated with impurity or exposure: the hammam (public bath) and cupping (hijama). The author cites two hadiths directly from the Prophet's practice to establish that such earnings are ja'iz. We will analyze the proofs and understand how the Hanafi school weighs them against counter-evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? Wages for hammam and cupping. What is the hukm? Ja'iz (permissible).
The text begins with a clear ruling statement.
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides two hadith: one from Ibn Umar about entering hammam with covering, and one from Ibn Abbas about the Prophet paying the cupper.
Both are ahad hadith, but considered strong enough for permissibility.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
For hammam: the hadith implies that entering with covering is allowed, so the service is permissible; thus wages for it are allowed. For cupping: the Prophet's action of paying establishes permissibility of taking wages.
The proof is direct (fi'l al-nabi) for cupping, and implicit (command with covering) for hammam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars prohibit cupping wages because of a hadith stating 'the earnings of the cupper are impure.' The Hanafi school responds that the Prophet's explicit action takes precedence.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position relies on the stronger evidence.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is permissibility, based on the explicit prophetic example, which overrides general disapproval.
The author notes that cupping is still not considered optimal, but the wage is halal.

[1205] (50) It is permissible to take wages for the bathhouse and cupping. It is permissible to take wages for hammam and cupping. In Europe, hammam means a specific type of bathhouse and swimming pool where some people bathe naked, but the wage is fixed and bathing with covering is impossible, so taking wages for it is permissible. (1) Since covering the body for bathing is impossible, giving wages for bathing is also permissible. (2) There is a hadith: From Abdullah ibn Umar, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'The lands of the non-Arabs will be conquered for you, and you will find houses called hammams. Men should not enter them except with an izaar, and prevent women from entering except a sick woman or one in nifas.' (Footnote a) (Abu Dawood, chapter on entering hammam, p. 200 no. 4011, Tirmidhi, chapter on entering hammam, vol. 2 p. 7 no. 28, Ibn Majah, chapter on entering hammam, p. 536 no. 3748) From this hadith it is known that men can enter hammam wearing a waist wrapper, so there is scope for taking and giving wages. And one can take wages for cupping; for this there is a hadith: From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Prophet got cupped and gave the cupper his wage. (Footnote b) (Bukhari, chapter on the earnings of the cupper, p. 304 no. 2278, Muslim, chapter on the permissibility of the wage of the cupper, p. 22 no. 1202) In this hadith, the Prophet himself got cupped and paid the wage, so taking and giving wages for cupping is permissible. However, since blood goes into the mouth from it, this act is not so good. Therefore, in some hadith, he prohibited it. The hadith is: From Rafi' ibn Khadij, that the Messenger of Allah said: 'The earnings of the cupper are impure.' (Abu Dawood, chapter on the earnings of the cupper, p. no. 342) Footnote: (a) He said: 'The lands of the non-Arabs will be conquered for you, and you will find houses called hammams. Men should not enter except with an izaar, and prevent women from entering except a sick woman or one in nifas, so she may enter for treatment.' (b) He got cupped and gave the cupper his wage.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of taking wages for using a hammam (bathhouse) and for cupping (hijama). The author begins by stating the ruling clearly: it is permissible. Then he provides the reasoning: in European contexts, hammams are often used naked, but since covering the body is impossible, the wage is for the service, not for the nudity. He supports with a hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar where the Prophet allows men to enter hammam with an izaar (waist wrapper), implying the service is permissible and thus wages for it are allowed. For cupping, he cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet himself paid the cupper, establishing permissibility. However, he notes a conflicting hadith that cupping earnings are impure because blood is involved, but the overall ruling remains permissible as the Prophet's action takes precedence. The footnote clarifies the hadiths. The passage concludes that despite some disapproval, the wage is allowed.

Key Terms
حمام (hammam): A public bathhouse, often with hot water and steam, where people bathe.
حجام (hajjam): A cupper: one who performs cupping therapy by drawing blood.
