Wet Nurse's Obligation to Prepare Child's Food
Ruling on wet nurse's obligation to prepare food for child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the wet nurse's duty regarding food preparation according to the Hanafi school and explain the role of custom ('urf) in determining contract obligations.

Core Idea
When a wet nurse's contract is silent, custom ('urf) determines if she must also prepare the child's food.

This lesson examines a ruling from the Hanafi school on the obligations of a wet nurse hired to breastfeed. The passage clarifies that, unless specified otherwise, the wet nurse is not limited to nursing alone—custom may require her to prepare the child's food as part of the wage. We will explore the evidence from the Quran and the reasoning behind relying on customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (preparing child's food) and the legal classification (wajib under certain conditions).
The ruling is not absolute; it depends on custom and contract specification.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the proof cited: Quran 2:236, which emphasizes giving provision according to custom (bil-ma'ruf).
The verse is used to support the validity of custom as a basis for obligations.
3
Understand the role of custom
Custom ('urf) fills contractual gaps. When the contract is silent, the prevailing custom defines the scope of duties.
Hanafi fiqh gives weight to 'urf in mu'amalat (transactions).
4
Apply to the wet nurse case
Default: if custom includes food preparation, it is wajib. Exception: if contract specifies only breastfeeding or custom excludes food prep, it is not wajib.
The ruling is conditional on both the absence of specification and the presence of custom.
5
Note the epistemological weight
This ruling is based on a combination of a Quranic principle (consideration of custom) and practical reasoning (istihsan). Its authority is derived from the Quran and accepted practice.
The ruling is considered mukhtalaf fih (disputed) across schools, but Hanafi relies on custom.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا خافوا على الصبي من لبنها وعليها أن تصلح طعام الصبي۔ دودھ پلانے والی انا اجرت کی وجہ سے دودھ تو پلائے گی ہی، بچے کو کھانے کی ضرورت ہوگی تو اس کا کھانا بنانا اورکھلانا اناہی کے ذمے ہیں۔ عرف میں دودھ پلانے کے ساتھ یہ دونوں کام اجرت میں شامل ہیں۔ یہ اس وقت ہے جب کام کی تصریح نہ ہو اور عرف میں کھانا بنانا اور کھلا نا اجرت میں شامل ہوں۔ لیکن اگر کام کی تصریح ہو جائے کہ صرف دودھ پلانا اجرت میں شامل ہے۔ یا عرف میں کھانا بنانا اور کھلا نا شامل نہ ہوں تو یہ دونوں کام اجرت میں شامل نہیں ہوں گے۔ اس کام کی تصریح نہ ہوتے وقت عرف کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ و متعوهن على الموسع قدره وعلى المقتر قدره متاعا بالمعروف حقا على المحسنين (ب) (آیت ۲۳۶ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں عرف عام کا اعتبار کیا گیا ہے۔ اس طرح انا کے کام کے بارے میں بھی تصریح نہ ہوتے وقت عرف عام کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ تصلح : اصلاح کرنا، یہاں مراد ہے کھانا بنانا۔
When they fear for the child from her milk, and it is upon her to prepare the child's food. The wet nurse will surely breastfeed due to the wage, but if the child needs food, preparing and feeding the food is also the responsibility of the wet nurse. In custom, along with breastfeeding, these two tasks are included in the wage. This is when the task is not specified and in custom preparing and feeding food are included in the wage. But if the task is specified that only breastfeeding is included in the wage, or in custom preparing and feeding food are not included, then these two tasks will not be included in the wage. When the task is not specified, custom will be considered. 'And give them a provision, the wealthy according to his means and the poor according to his means, a provision according to custom, a duty upon the doers of good.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:236) In this verse, general custom is considered. Similarly, regarding the wet nurse's work, when there is no specification, general custom will be considered. 'Taslih': to repair, here meaning to prepare food.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This is a ruling about the obligations of a wet nurse hired for breastfeeding. The text states that if there is a fear that the child may be harmed by the wet nurse's milk (e.g., insufficient or harmful), then she is required to prepare the child's food (solid food) in addition to breastfeeding. The commentary explains that according to custom ('urf), the wet nurse's job includes both breastfeeding and preparing/feeding food to the child. This is the default when the contract does not specify otherwise. If the contract specifies only breastfeeding, or if custom does not include food preparation, then those tasks are not included. The Quranic verse (2:236) is cited to support the consideration of custom ('urf) in determining obligations. The verse instructs to provide for divorced women according to custom, indicating that custom is a valid source for determining what is appropriate. Therefore, the wet nurse must prepare the child's food, and this is part of the hired service unless the contract or local custom says otherwise.

Key Terms
عرف (urf): Customary practice that is prevalent and accepted in society, used to determine default obligations in contracts when not specified.
تصلح (tuslih): To make right or repair; here specifically meaning to prepare food.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The wet nurse's preference
C) The child's age
D) The judge's opinion

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, custom ('urf) fills contractual gaps; thus a wet nurse must prepare food if local custom includes it and the contract does not specify otherwise.

No Wage for Wet Nurse Who Feeds Goat's Milk Instead
Ruling with proof: wet nurse's breach of condition voids wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wet nurse violates a condition to breastfeed with her own milk, and apply the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' to derive the consequence.

Core Idea
Breaching a specific condition in a service contract forfeits the agreed wage.

This lesson examines a Hanafi ruling on hire (ijara) where the employee deviates from a stipulated condition. The case involves a wet nurse hired to breastfeed with her own milk, but she feeds goat's milk instead. The text uses the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' (Bukhari) to argue that she loses the contractual wage, though she may receive compensation for the actual service rendered.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The wet nurse substitutes her own milk with goat's milk. The ruling: she does not receive the agreed wage for breastfeeding, but may be compensated for the actual service (feeding) she performed.
The ruling distinguishes between the contractual wage (for a specific service) and compensation for a different service.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'المسلمون عند شروطهم' (Muslims are bound by their conditions), recorded by Bukhari no. 2274.
This hadith is a general principle in Hanafi muamalat.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The condition in the contract was to breastfeed with her own milk. By feeding goat's milk, the wet nurse violated this condition. The hadith obliges fulfillment of conditions, so she loses entitlement to the specified wage.
The wage was tied to the condition; breach nullifies that entitlement.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) might award the full wage if the child benefits, but the Hanafi school focuses on the breach of condition regardless of benefit.
The Hanafi view prioritizes contractual terms over mere benefit.
5
Determine the thamarah
Practically, the wet nurse receives only compensation for her actual work (feeding goat's milk) at market rate, not the agreed wage for breastfeeding.
This protects the specificity of conditions in service contracts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ارضعته في المدة بلبن شاة فلا اجرة لها۔ مثلا سال بھر کے لئے انا کو دودھ پلانے کے لئے اجرت پر لیا اور انا نے اپنا دودھ پلانے کے بجائے بکری کا دودھ پلاتی رہی تو اس کو دودھ پلانے کی اجرت نہیں ملے گی۔ اجرت اپنا دودھ پلانے کی تھی بکری کا دودھ پلانے کی نہیں ۔ یہ تو بچے کے والدین بھی کر سکتے تھے اس لئے اس کو دودھ پلانے کی اجرت نہیں ملے گی۔ البتہ جو خدمت کی ہے اس کی اجرت مل جائے گی۔ اسوان شرط کی مخالفت کرے تو اجرت نہیں ملے گی۔ حدیث میں ہے المسلمون عند شروطهم (الف) ( بخاری شریف نمبر ۲۲۷۴) حاشیہ : (الف) رافع بن خدیج کو سونے اور چاندی کے بدلے زمین کو کرایہ پر لینے کے بارے میں پوچھا، فرمایا کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے۔ لوگ حضور کے زمانے میں اجرت پر لیتے تھے اونچی جگہ اور نالی کے کنارے اور کاشتکاری میں سے خاص حصے کی شرط پر ۔ پس ہلاک ہوتا تھا یہ اور محفوظ رہتا تھاوہ، اور محفوظر ہتا تھا یہ اور ہلاک ہوتا تھا وہ ۔ پس نہیں ہوتا تھا لوگوں کے لئے کرایہ مگر یہ اس لئے حضور نے اس سے منع فرمایا، بہر حال معلوم چیز کے بدلے تو کوئی حرج کی بات نہیں ہے (ب) فائدہ دو عورتوں کو مالدار پر اس کے مناسب اور غریب پر اس کے مناسب فائدہ اٹھانے دیتا ہے معروف طریقے پر ا یہ حق ہے اچھے کام کرنے والوں پر ۔
And if she breastfeeds him during the period with the milk of a goat, then there is no wage for her. For example, a wet nurse was hired for one year to breastfeed, and instead of her own milk, she fed the child goat's milk, then she will not get the wage for breastfeeding. The wage was for her own milk, not for feeding goat's milk. This task could have been done by the child's parents, so she will not get the wage for breastfeeding. However, she will be paid for the service she actually rendered. If she violates the condition, she will not get the wage. The hadith says: 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' (Bukhari no. 2274) Footnote: (a) Rafe' bin Khadeej was asked about leasing land for gold and silver; he said there is no harm. People used to lease during the Prophet's time on condition of elevated areas and edges of streams and specific portions of cultivation; then one would perish and another would be safe, etc. so he forbade it. But for something known and guaranteed, there is no harm. (b) Benefit: Give the two women benefit according to the capacity of the wealthy and the poor, a benefit according to custom, a duty upon the doers of good.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This ruling states that a wet nurse who substitutes her own milk with goat's milk during the contracted period loses her right to the wage. The commentary explains that the wage was specifically for her own milk; feeding goat's milk is a breach of contract because the parents could have done that themselves. The wet nurse will only be paid for the service she actually performed (e.g., feeding), but not the agreed wage for breastfeeding. The principle from the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' is invoked: by violating the condition (to breastfeed with her own milk), she forfeits the wage. The footnote narrates a hadith about leasing land, illustrating that specified conditions must be followed; if the lease is for a known sum, it is permissible, but ambiguous conditions that lead to uncertainty are prohibited. This reinforces the importance of adhering to stipulated terms.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition stipulated in the contract; here, that the wet nurse breastfeed with her own milk.
اجرة (ujrah): Wage or payment for service; in this context, the agreed payment for breastfeeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A condition stipulated in a service contract is binding; violating it forfeits the agreed wage, but compensation for actual service may be due.

Artisan with Visible Effect May Retain Object for Wage
Ruling on artisan's retention right due to attached property

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an artisan's right to retain an object until payment and identify the condition that triggers this right.

Core Idea
An artisan whose work leaves a physical effect may retain the object until paid, because his own property is attached.

This passage from the Hanafi text addresses a practical issue in muamalat: an artisan who has added his own materials (like dye or soap) to a customer’s object. The ruling grants him a lien-like right to hold the object until his wage is paid. Understanding this right requires recognizing the key condition — a tangible effect (athar fi al-'ayn) — and the underlying reasoning based on ownership of attached property.

Guided Path
1
Identify the artisan category
Who is included in this ruling? Only those whose work leaves a visible effect on the object, such as a dyer or washerman.
A purely service provider like a porter is excluded.
2
State the legal right
What can such an artisan do? He may retain the object after completing his work until he receives his wage.
This is a right (haqq), not an obligation.
3
Note the condition
What triggers the right? The work must leave an effect (athar) on the object itself.
The effect must be tangible and attributable to the artisan's materials.
4
Understand the rationale
Why is retention allowed? The artisan's own property (dye, soap) becomes attached to the object, so he may detain the whole object to secure payment.
This is based on the principle that one can retain one's own property.
5
Apply to a new case
A tailor stitches a cloth using his own thread. Does the right apply? Yes, because the thread is attached and leaves an effect.
If the thread is provided by the customer, the right may not apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل صانع لعمله اثر في العين كالقصار والصباغ فله ان يحبس العين بعد الفراغ من عمله حتى يستوفى الاجرة۔ جن جن کار دیگر کا عمل عین شی میں اثر انداز ہوتا ہو جیسے رنگریز کامل کہ کپڑے کو اپنے رنگ سے رنگ دیتا ہے اور کپڑا رنگین ہو جاتا ہے یا دھوبی کا عمل کہ اپنے سوڈے اور صابن سے کپڑے کو صاف کرتا ہے اور ان کے عمل کا اثر کپڑوں میں ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ ایسے کاریگروں کو حق ہے کہ کام پورا کرنے کے بعد اجرت لینے کے لئے اس چیز کو اپنے پاس روک لے اور جب تک اجرت وصول نہ کرے کپڑا واپس نہ دے۔ مثلا رنگریز کا رنگ اپنا ہے، دھوبی کا صابن اور سوڈا اپنا ہے اس لئے اپنی چیز روکنے کا حق ہے۔ اور چونکہ یہ چیزیں کپڑے کے ساتھ چپکی ہوئی ہیں اس لئے کپڑا بھی روک لے گا۔ تا کہ پوری اجرت وصول ہو جائے۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اپنی چیز کو روک سکتا ہے اس لئے جس چیز کے ساتھ چپکی ہوئی ہے اس کو بھی روک سکتا ہے۔
And every artisan whose work leaves an effect in the object, like the washerman and the dyer, has the right to retain the object after completing his work until he receives his wage. Whatever craftsman's work affects the object itself, like the dyer who dyes the cloth with his color and the cloth becomes colored, or the washerman's work who cleans the cloth with his soap and soda, and the effect of their work appears in the cloth. Such craftsmen have the right, after finishing the work, to keep the object with themselves to collect the wage, and until they receive the wage, they will not return the cloth. For example, the dyer's color is his own, the washerman's soap and soda are his own, so he has the right to retain his own property. And since these things are attached to the cloth, he will also retain the cloth so that the full wage is received. This ruling is based on the principle that one can retain one's own property, and therefore one can also retain the thing to which it is attached.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This ruling establishes a right of retention (habs) for artisans whose work leaves a visible effect on the object, such as a dyer (who adds color) or a washerman (who cleans with his own materials). They may detain the object after finishing the work until the customer pays the wage. The reasoning is that these artisans have added their own property (dye, soap) to the object, which becomes attached. Since they have a right to their property, they may retain the object as security until payment. This is akin to a lien. The commentary emphasizes that the artisan's own materials are affixed to the object, so detaining the object is a means to secure payment. This right is only for those whose work leaves a physical effect; if the work is purely service without such effect, the artisan does not have this right.

Key Terms
حبس العين (habs al-'ayn): The act of retaining the physical object (e.g., cloth) as security until payment is received.
أثر في العين (athar fi al-'ayn): A tangible effect on the object itself, such as dyeing or washing that changes the object's appearance or quality.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following artisans has the right to retain the object after work until payment?
A) A tailor who stitches cloth (work leaves effect - stitching)
B) A porter who carries goods
C) A painter who paints a wall (work leaves effect - paint)
D) A teacher who tutors a child

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school grants artisans a right of retention (habs) only when their work leaves a physical effect on the object, based on the principle that they may detain their own property attached to it.

Artisan Without Visible Effect Cannot Retain Object
Ruling that artisans without effect have no right to retain object

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for artisans without effect and identify the exception based on necessity.

Core Idea
Work that leaves no effect on the object gives no right to retain it for payment.

In the previous lesson, we saw that artisans whose work leaves a visible effect (like a tailor) can retain the object until paid. But what about porters or boatmen who simply move goods? Their labor leaves no trace. This lesson clarifies that they cannot detain the property for their wages. However, there is a crucial exception when the legal system fails, allowing them to protect their right to payment.

Guided Path
1
Name the act and its category
Identify the act being ruled upon: retaining an object for unpaid wages. This falls under Ijarah (hire) and the concept of lien (habs).
2
Identify the hukm level
Determine the ruling: normally it is not permissible (la yajuz) for an artisan without effect to retain the object.
The hukm is based on the lack of a property right attached to the object.
3
Recognize the key condition
The condition for having a right to retain is that the work must leave a tangible effect on the object (e.g., stitching, dyeing). Without this effect, there is no right.
This condition distinguishes this case from the previous lesson.
4
Note the exception for necessity
When the judiciary is inaccessible and there is a real fear of losing the wage, the worker may retain the object as an exception. This is based on necessity (darurah).
The exception allows retention only until payment; it does not create a permanent right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن ليس لعمله اثر في العين فليس له ان يحبس العين للاجرة كالحمال والملاح۔ جس کا عمل اور نفع ایسا ہے کہ اس کے عمل کا اثر عین شی میں نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسے بوجھ اٹھانے والے کے عمل کا اثر سامان میں نہیں ہوتا ، وہ تو صرف سامان کو اٹھا کر ادھر سے ادھر کر دیا۔ اس کے اٹھانے کا کوئی اثر سامان پر نہیں پڑتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ اپنی اجرت وصول کرنے کے لئے سامان کو اپنے پاس قانونی طور پر نہیں رکھ سکتا۔ چونکہ بوجھ اٹھانے والے کی اپنی کوئی چیز سامان کے ساتھ محبوس نہیں ہے اس لئے دوسرے کے سامان کو روکنے کا حق اس کو نہیں ہوگا۔ اگر اجرت نہ دے تو قاضی کے پاس مقدمہ دائر کر سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اس دور میں چونکہ قاضی آسانی سے دستیاب نہی ہے اس لئے سامان سے دستیاب نہی۔ جانے کے بعد اجرت ملنے کی امید نہ ہو تو سامان روک لے تا کہ اجرت بآسانی مل سکے۔
And the one whose work has no effect in the object, he does not have the right to retain the object for the wage, like the porter and the boatman. The one whose work and benefit is such that his work has no effect on the object itself, like the porter's work has no effect on the goods; he just moves the goods from one place to another. His lifting leaves no effect on the goods. Therefore, he cannot legally keep the goods with himself to collect his wage. Since the porter has no property of his own attached to the goods, he has no right to retain another's goods. If the wage is not given, he can file a case with the judge. However, in this era, since the judge is not easily accessible, if after the goods are delivered there is no hope of receiving the wage, he may retain the goods to facilitate collection of the wage.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This ruling is the counterpart to the previous one. It states that artisans whose work does not leave a tangible effect on the object—such as a porter or boatman who simply transports goods without altering them—do not have the right to detain the object for payment. The reason is that they have not added any of their own property to the object, so there is no basis for a lien. Their remedy is to take the matter to a judge. The commentary adds a practical note: in times when judges are not accessible, if there is fear of losing the wage, the porter may retain the goods as a precaution to secure payment. This is an exception based on necessity, but the general rule is that such workers cannot detain the object.

Key Terms
حمال (hammal): A porter or carrier who transports goods without altering them.
ملاح (mallah): A boatman who transports goods or people by water; his work similarly does not leave a physical effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why cannot a porter retain the goods he transported for unpaid wages?
A) Because his work is not completed
B) Because his work leaves no effect on the goods
C) Because he is not an artisan
D) Because the goods are too heavy

Key Takeaway
Workers whose labor leaves no trace on the object cannot legally detain it for payment; they must seek a judge's help, except when the judiciary is unavailable.

Artisan Must Perform Work Personally if Stipulated
Ruling on condition of personal performance in ijara

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when an artisan is required by contract to work personally and identify the consequence of delegating to another.

Core Idea
A valid condition in a contract is binding; if personal work is stipulated, delegation is prohibited.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in service contracts (ijara): a hirer explicitly requires a specific artisan to perform the work. When such a condition is made, the artisan cannot delegate the task to someone else. The ruling is grounded in the general principle that Muslims must honour their contractual conditions, as established by the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' Understanding this ruling helps you appreciate the importance of explicit terms in Islamic contract law and the consequences of violating them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contractual condition
Look at the contract: has the hirer explicitly stipulated that the artisan himself must do the work? The condition must be valid and consistent with the nature of the contract.
The condition here is 'you must work yourself' — this is a valid stipulation.
2
Determine the ruling on delegation
Once the condition is established, the artisan cannot employ another person to do the work. Delegation would violate the condition and is therefore not permissible.
The ruling is that delegation is haram when it breaches a valid condition.
3
Understand the evidence
The hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' (al-muslimun 'ala shurutihim) provides the basis for enforcing such stipulations. Conditions that are not contrary to shari'ah must be fulfilled.
This is a general principle in fiqh mu'amalat.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If the artisan delegates despite the condition, the hirer may have the right to rescind the contract or refuse payment. The artisan may forfeit the wage if the condition was material.
The exact consequence may depend on whether the condition was essential (shart lazim) and the extent of harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اشترط على الصانع ان يعمل بنفسه فلا يجوز له ان يستعمل غيره۔ اگر شرط لگائی کا ریگر پر یہ کہ وہ خود کرے گا تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ استعمال کرے دوسرے کو۔ کام کرانے والے نے شرط لگائی کہ مثلا زید ہی اس کام کو انجام دے گا تو اب زید کے لئے یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ عمر سے کام کروا کر دے (ب) مسلمان اپنی شرطوں کے پاسبان ہیں۔
And if a condition is made upon the artisan that he will work himself, then it is not permissible for him to employ another. If a condition is placed that, for example, Zaid himself will do the work, then Zaid does not have the right to have Umar do the work and give it. (b) Muslims are bound by their conditions.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This ruling addresses a situation where a hirer stipulates that a specific artisan (e.g., Zaid) must perform the work personally. In such a case, the artisan cannot delegate the work to another person (e.g., Umar). The contractual condition is binding based on the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions.' The commentary notes that this is consistent with the principle that conditions in contracts must be fulfilled. The hirer's reliance on the artisan's personal skill or trust is a valid consideration. If the artisan violates the condition, the contract may be affected.

Key Terms
اشتراط (ishtirat): The act of imposing a condition in a contract; here, specifying that the artisan himself must do the work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) No, because the condition requires personal work
C) Yes, if the apprentice is equally skilled
D) No, unless the customer agrees later

Key Takeaway
If a contract stipulates personal performance, the artisan cannot delegate; violating the condition is prohibited and may invalidate the contract.

Right to Detain the Object: Effect vs. No Effect
States when a craftsman may detain the object for wage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a craftsman may detain an object for unpaid wages and distinguish between workers whose work leaves an effect on the object and those who do not.

Core Idea
Only a craftsman whose work leaves a physical effect on the object may detain it for his wage.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text on ijarah (hire) addresses a practical problem: can a worker hold onto the customer's property until paid? The answer depends on whether the worker's effort leaves a lasting trace on the item. This lesson will clarify the distinction and its legal basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of workers
The text mentions two categories: those whose work has an effect on the object (e.g., washerman, dyer) and those whose work has no effect (e.g., porter, boatman).
Effect means a physical change or addition, like dye or soap.
2
Understand the legal consequence for each category
The first category has the right to detain the object until paid; the second does not.
The right is a legal entitlement, not an obligation.
3
Identify the underlying principle
The right arises because the craftsman mixes his own property (dye, soap) with the object, giving him a lien over the combined item.
Without mixing property, there is no basis for detention.
4
Apply the distinction to a new scenario
Consider a tailor who uses his own thread: his work leaves an effect (stitches) using his property, so he may detain. A porter merely moves goods without altering them, so he may not.
The key is whether the worker's own materials become part of the object.
5
Recognize the practical outcome
The rule provides a security for the craftsman's wage when he has invested his own property, while protecting the customer's property from being held arbitrarily.
In modern contexts, the principle can extend to mechanics using their own parts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل صانع لعمله اثر في العين كالقصار والصباغ فله ان يحبس العين بعد الفراغ من عمله حتى يستوفى الاجرة (۲۲) ومن ليس لعمله اثر في العين فليس له ان يحبس العين للاجرة كالحمال والملاح [۱۲۱۶] (۲۱) ہر وہ کاریگر جس کے عمل کا اثر عین میں ہو جیسے دھوبی اور رنگریز تو اس کو حق ہے کہ عین کو روک رکھے عمل سے فارغ ہونے کے بعد یہاں تک کہ اجرت لے لے۔ جن جن کار دیگر کا عمل عین شی میں اثر انداز ہوتا ہو جیسے رنگریز کامل کہ کپڑے کو اپنے رنگ سے رنگ دیتا ہے اور کپڑا رنگین ہو جاتا ہے یا دھوبی کا عمل کہ اپنے سوڈے اور صابن سے کپڑے کو صاف کرتا ہے اور ان کے عمل کا اثر کپڑوں میں ظاہر ہوتا ہے۔ ایسے کاریگروں کو حق ہے کہ کام پورا کرنے کے بعد اجرت لینے کے لئے اس چیز کو اپنے پاس روک لے اور جب تک اجرت وصول نہ کرے کپڑا واپس نہ دے۔ مثلا رنگریز کا رنگ اپنا ہے، دھوبی کا صابن اور سوڈا اپنا ہے اس لئے اپنی چیز روکنے کا حق ہے۔ اور چونکہ یہ چیزیں کپڑے کے ساتھ چپکی ہوئی ہیں اس لئے کپڑا بھی روک لے گا۔ تا کہ پوری اجرت وصول ہو جائے۔ یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اپنی چیز کو روک سکتا ہے اس لئے جس چیز کے ساتھ چپکی ہوئی ہے اس کو بھی روک سکتا ہے۔ [۱۲۱۷) (۶۲) اور جس کے عمل کا اثر نہیں ہے عین شی میں تو اس کے لئے حق نہیں ہے کہ کہ رو کے عین شی کو اجرت کے لئے جیسے بوجھ اٹھانے والا اور ملاح۔ جس کا عمل اور نفع ایسا ہے کہ اس کے عمل کا اثر عین شی میں نہیں ہوتا۔ جیسے بوجھ اٹھانے والے کے عمل کا اثر سامان میں نہیں ہوتا ، وہ تو صرف سامان کو اٹھا کر ادھر سے ادھر کر دیا۔ اس کے اٹھانے کا کوئی اثر سامان پر نہیں پڑتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ اپنی اجرت وصول کرنے کے لئے سامان کو اپنے پاس قانونی طور پر نہیں رکھ سکتا۔ چونکہ بوجھ اٹھانے والے کی اپنی کوئی چیز سامان کے ساتھ محبوس نہیں ہے اس لئے دوسرے کے سامان کو روکنے کا حق اس کو نہیں ہوگا۔ اگر اجرت نہ دے تو قاضی کے پاس مقدمہ دائر کر سکتا ہے۔ البتہ اس دور میں چونکہ قاضی آسانی سے دستیاب نہی ہے اس لئے سامان سے دستیاب نہی۔ جانے کے بعد اجرت ملنے کی امید نہ ہو تو سامان روک لے تا کہ اجرت بآسانی مل سکے۔
Every craftsman whose work has an effect on the object, like the washerman and the dyer, has the right to detain the object after finishing his work until he receives his wage. (22) And whoever's work has no effect on the object has no right to detain the object for the wage, like the porter and the boatman. [1216] (21) Every craftsman whose work's effect is in the object, like washerman and dyer, he has the right to detain the object after finishing the work until he takes the wage. ... [1217] (62) And he whose work has no effect in the object has no right to detain the object for the wage, like the porter and the boatman. ...
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage presents two contrasting rulings. The first ruling states that a craftsman whose work leaves a physical effect on the object (e.g., a dyer changes the color, a washerman cleans with his soap) may detain that object after completing his work until he receives his wage. This is because he has mixed his own property (dye, soap) with the object, giving him a right of retention. The second ruling states that a craftsman whose work has no lasting effect on the object (e.g., a porter simply moves goods, a boatman transports items) cannot detain the object for unpaid wages. If not paid, he must take the matter to court. However, in contemporary times when courts are not easily accessible, he may detain the object as a practical measure.

Key Terms
الاجارة (al-ijarah): A contract of hire or lease; the subject of the chapter.
العين (al-ayn): The physical object that is worked upon (e.g., cloth).
حبس (habs): Detaining physically for security of payment.
أثر (athar): Physical effect; a change or addition made to the object by the craftsman's work using his own materials.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A porter who carried goods from one place to another
B) A washerman who cleaned clothes with his own soap
C) A boatman who transported goods across a river
D) A farmer who harvested the customer's crop

Key Takeaway
A craftsman may detain an object for his wage only if his work leaves a physical effect using his own property; otherwise, he must seek payment through the court.

Stipulation of Personal Performance
Ruling when worker is stipulated to work himself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a hired worker may not delegate the work when the employer stipulates personal performance, and cite the hadith that proves this.

Core Idea
A condition in a contract is binding; delegation violates the agreement.

When hiring a craftsman, the employer may stipulate that a specific person must perform the work. This condition, like all valid conditions, must be honored. The hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' provides the legal basis. In this lesson, we examine why delegation becomes impermissible under such a stipulation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The employer stipulates that the worker (e.g., Zaid) must do the work himself. This is a condition in the ijarah contract.
2
State the ruling
It is not permissible (haram) for Zaid to employ another person to do the work. He must perform it himself.
3
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'المسلمون عند شروطهم' (Muslims are bound by their conditions). This is a general principle.
4
Apply the dalil
The condition that Zaid works himself is binding. Delegation would violate this condition, so it is prohibited.
5
Consequence
If Zaid delegates, the employer can reject the work and may not be liable for the wage until the condition is fulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا اشترط على الصانع ان يعمل بنفسه فليس له ان يستعمل غيره [۱۲۱۸] (۶۳) اگر شرط لگائی کا ریگر پر یہ کہ وہ خود کرے گا تو اس کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ استعمال کرے دوسرے کو۔ کام کرانے والے نے شرط لگائی کہ مثلا زید ہی اس کام کو انجام دے گا تو اب زید کے لئے یہ حق نہیں ہے کہ عمر سے کام کروا کر دے (ب) مسلمان اپنی شرطوں کے پاسبان ہیں۔ [۲۴] وان اطلق له العمل فله ان يستأجر من يعمله [۱۲۱۹) (۶۴) اور اگر اجیر کے لئے عمل مطلق چھوڑا تو اس کے لئے جائز ہے کہ نوکر پر رکھے اس کو جو وہ کام کرے۔ اگر یوں شرط نہیں لگائی کہ مثلا زیدی کو کام کرنا ہے تو اجیر کے لئے جائز ہے کہ کسی اور سے کام کروا کر مستاجر کو نفع سپر د کر دے۔ کسی کام کرنے والے کو خاص نہیں کیا تو اس کا مطلب یہ ہوا کہ مستاجر کو کام اچھا چاہئے چاہے کوئی بھی اس کام کو کر دے۔ اس لئے اجیر خود بھی اس کام کو کرے تب بھی ٹھیک ہے اور دوسرں سے کروا کر دے تب بھی ٹھیک ہے۔ وہ سپر د کر نے پر اجرت کا مستحق ہوگا۔ صرف کام مقصود ہو تو کسی آدمی سے بھی وہ کام کروا سکتا ہے۔
And if it is stipulated upon the craftsman that he work himself, then he may not employ another [1218] (63) If a condition is made that the worker himself will do it, then it is not permissible for him to use another. The employer made a condition that, for example, Zaid will do this work, so Zaid does not have the right to have Umar do it and give it. Muslims are bound by their conditions. [24] And if the work is left absolute for him, then he may hire someone to do it. [1219] (64) And if the work is left absolute for the hired worker, then it is permissible for him to hire another to do the work. If no condition was made, e.g., that Zaid must do the work, then the hired worker may have someone else do the work and deliver the benefit to the employer. The employer wants good work, whoever does it. So it is fine whether the hired worker does it himself or gets another. He becomes entitled to wage upon delivery.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage covers two related rulings. First: If the employer explicitly stipulates that a specific worker (e.g., Zaid) must perform the work himself, that worker cannot delegate the job to someone else. The legal basis is the hadith 'Muslims are bound by their conditions' (al-Muslimun 'ala shurutihim). Second: If the contract is absolute (no stipulation regarding who performs), the worker may either do the work himself or hire another person to do it. The employer's interest is in the completion of the work, not necessarily the identity of the worker. The worker is entitled to the wage upon delivery of the completed work.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition stipulated in the contract of hire.
اطلاق (itlaq): Leaving the work unrestricted without stipulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Permissible, as long as the work is done well
B) Not permissible, because the condition must be honored
C) Permissible only if the apprentice is equally skilled
D) Not permissible unless the employer agrees later

Key Takeaway
A valid condition in an ijarah contract must be fulfilled; delegating work when personal performance is stipulated is not permissible.

Absolute Contract: Delegation Permitted
Ruling when work is left absolute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that when an ijarah contract does not specify who must perform the work, the hired worker may delegate the task to another person.

Core Idea
Without a stipulation, the worker's obligation is to deliver the result, not to personally perform.

When the employer does not restrict who must do the work, the hired worker has discretion. He may perform the work himself or hire another to do it. The employer's interest lies in the completed work, not the identity of the worker. This lesson examines the ruling for such absolute contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The contract is absolute; no condition is placed on who performs the work.
2
State the ruling
The worker may hire another person to do the work. It is permissible (ja'iz).
3
Apply the default rule
Since no condition restricts delegation, the default principle of permissibility (ibaha) applies.
4
Consequence
The worker is entitled to the wage upon delivering the completed work to the employer.
